出自tedxboston這個開放的演講中 , 理查德・雷斯尼克告訴我們基因測序是如何廉價並快速得顛覆醫療體制 。	in the opening speech since tedxboston , richard resnick has told us how gene sequencing is cheap and rapidly subvert health care systems .
dna , biotech , healthcare , science , technology	dna , biome , tech , healthcare , thumbs well .
理查德・雷斯尼克:歡迎進入基因革命時代	richard resnick: welcome into the genomic revolution .
女士們先生們 , 我向您展示人類基因組	ladies and gentlemen , i'm going to show you the human genome .
左上是一號染色體	upper left is a chromosome called chromosome .

因此我們要匯入含有新的載荷方向的新的力	so we're going to embrace new forces with new charge directions .
在匯入新方向的時候我們要猜測在這個方向上粒子帶有什麼樣的載荷然後我們就能讓它和其他粒子一起旋轉	and when we introduce a new direction , we have to guess what charges the particles have in this direction , and we can rotate it with the other particles .
如果猜對的話我們就可以在六維載荷空間中構造標準載荷集作為更完美的七維載荷空間圖案的非對稱子集	and if we guess right , we can construct the standard charges in sixdimensional charge spaces as a perfect symmetry of the sevendimensional charge
這種粒子選擇方法由帕蒂和薩拉姆在1973年提出它是大統一理論的一種探索	this is a method of particle choice , proposed by patie and salaam in 1973 , and it's a kind of exploration of the unified theory .
在我們看到這個新的合成圖案時發現有些空間應該有粒子卻空出來了	as we saw this new synthetic pattern , we found that there are spaces that ought to be particles but empty .
這是統一理論的研究方式	this is the way the theory of unification works .
物理學家將已有的結構作為子集探索更大更對稱的結構	physicists will go on to explore larger , more symmetrical structures as subsets .
這個更大的結構可以讓我們預測那些實際存在卻沒有被觀察到的粒子	this larger configuration allows us to predict the existence of particles that are not yet observed .
這個統一模型推測出了這兩種新子對應的粒子它們應該和弱力很相似但是效果更弱	this unification proves that these two new particles should be very similar to the weak force , but it's much weaker .
現在可以在七維空間中旋轉這個載荷集同時考慮一下關於粒子的奇怪現象:在六維載荷空間中物質的第二代和第三代擁有和第一代物質相同的載荷	now you can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider the strange phenomenon of particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space .
這些粒子透過對應的六個載荷無法一一識別	these particles can't identify with six charges corresponding to each other .
在標準載荷空間上他們會彼此疊加	in the standard charge space , they superimposition each other .
然而在八維載荷空間中我們可以賦予每一個粒子唯一的新載荷	but in eightdimensional charge space , we can get every single particle , except for new charges .
然後在八維空間中旋轉看看整體的圖案是什麼樣的	and then you rotate around in eight dimensions and see what the overall pattern looks like .
這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代透過一種叫 " 三重性 " 對稱和第一代相關聯	here we see the second and third generations of matter associated with first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "
在八維中的這個特殊的載荷圖案是數學中最為漂亮的幾何結構之一	this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is one of the most beautiful geometric structures in mathematics .
這是最大的例外型李群e8的圖案	this is the largest exceptional lie group , the e8 .
李群是光滑曲線形的248維空間	the lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .
圖案的每一點都能這個極其複雜而又美麗的圖案中找到對稱點	each point in this pattern can find symmetry in this very complicated and beautiful pattern .
e8中的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中用來解釋重力的扭曲時空	a small part of e8 can be used to describe einstein's general theory of relativity to explain the distortion of gravity .
這個幾何形狀和量子力學一起能夠以最小的尺度描述萬物之理	this geometry , along with quantum mechanics , is able to describe everything at the smallest scales .
而在八維載荷空間中的這個圖案顯得異常美麗它還囊括了上千種這些基本粒子之間可能的相互作用每一種作用只是這個複雜形狀的一個平面	and the pattern in the eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it also captures thousands of interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just one flat surface to this complicated shape .
轉動它時可以看到包含其中的很多錯綜複雜的圖案	as you spin it , you can see many intricate patterns containing this intricate pattern .
透過某種旋轉我們可以在八維空間沿一個對稱軸方向觀察這個圖案並且一次看盡所有粒子	and with a kind of rotation , we can look at this pattern in the eightdimensional axis of the symmetry and see all the particles at once .
這是個很美的結構和其他統一理論一樣我們可以看到在這個圖案中有一些空格需要新的粒子來填補	it's a beautiful structure , and like any unifying theory , we can see that there's some space in this pattern that needs new particles to fill .
在這有20個空格需要新粒子來填補其中兩個已有帕蒂和薩拉姆粒子填補	here , 20 gaps need new particles to fill in , two of which have been filled with paraaty and sarah particles .
從圖案的位置我們知道這些新粒子和希格斯粒子一樣存在於標量場中但是它們擁有色荷且和強力相互作用	from the position of the pattern , we know that these new particles , like the higgs particles , are in the quantum field , but they have color charge and interact with the strong force .
填入這些新粒子使圖案完整讓我們得到完整的e8	filling in these new particles complete the patterns , giving us the full e8 .
這個e8圖案有著深厚的數學根基	this e8 pattern has deep mathematical roots .
在數學界中它被很多人認為是最美麗的結構	in mathematics , it's thought to be the most beautiful structure .
有人預言這個擁有無比數學美的結構能夠以我們可以想象到的最小尺寸描述粒子相互作用的真相	it's predicted that this mathematical beauty is supposed to describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales we can imagine .
而這個數學描述自然的理論並不是剛剛出來的	and this mathematical description of nature isn't new .
1623年伽利略寫道: " 大自然這本一直展示在我們面前的書是用數學的語言寫的	in 1623 , galileo wrote , " nature , this kept demonstrating that the book in front of us was written in mathematics .
它由三角形圓形和其他幾何形狀組成沒有了這些東西在人力所及的範圍裡我們根本不能瞭解沒有了這些我們會迷失在黑暗的迷宮中 "	it consists of triangle circles and other geometric shapes without these things in the human labor and we don't know at all that without these , we're going to get lost in the dark labyrinths . "
我相信這是真的我曾試過按照伽利略的指導只用三角形圓形和其他的幾何形狀去描述量子物理的數學性	i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of quantum physics in triangles and other geometric shapes .
當我和其他物理學家在研究這些東西時數學就像一個黑暗的迷宮	when i'm working with other physicists , mathematics is like a dark labyrinth .
但是我們確信數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學	but we're convinced that the core of mathematics is purely beautiful geometry .
數學和量子力學一起把我們的宇宙描述為一個在成長的e8珊瑚同時粒子在每個可能的位置相互作用展現出美麗的圖案	mathematics and quantum mechanics describe our universe as a growing e8 coral , and particles interact in all positions and display beautiful patterns .
藉助大型強子對撞機之類的新型機器圖案得到進一步豐富我們可能看到到底e8圖案還是另一種圖案反映了自然的本質	further patterns are further abundant in the patterns of new machines like the large hadron collider , and we might see that there's an e8 pattern or a different pattern that reflects what nature is .
這個探索過程是一個奇妙的探險	and this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure .
如果對撞機發現了符合e8圖案的粒子那可太酷了	if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that's really cool .
如果對撞機發現了新粒子但不符合這個圖案那會非常有趣雖然對e8理論不利	if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern , it's going to be interesting , although bad for e8 theory .
而且在一定程度上對我不利	and to some extent , it's bad for me .
那到底有多不利呢 ?	so how bad would that be ?
恩那是十分的不利啊	well , that's bad .
但推測大自然的運作總是很冒險的	but it's always very risky to predict how nature works .
這個理論和其他這型別的理論都是在下大注	this theory and all of these others are getting shots .
即使花很多精力取得很多成果也不一定能得出自然的真理	and even if you spend a lot of energy gaining , you don't necessarily have a natural truth .
理論物理就是這樣失敗是很常見的	that's how theoretical physics is failing quite a lot .
這樣看來新物理理論就像新開的公司	so , new theories of physics look like startup companies .
巨大投資後對那些失敗的嘗試情感上總會難以割捨	it's very hard for any attempts to get rid of after a huge investment in those failures .
但在科學界如果沒有用就要丟掉它再試試別的	but in science , if it's not going to work , throw it away , try something else .
而在這些不確定中唯一能夠保持理智並獲得幸福的方法是在生活中保持平衡和明察事理	and the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in these uncertain ways is to keep balance and perspective in life .
我已經儘可能保持生活的平衡了	i've been trying to keep my life balanced .
我試著在物理愛情和衝浪中尋找平衡就是我三個載荷的方向	i'm trying to balance my physics with love and surfing , and that's my three charge direction .
這樣就算我的物理研究沒有任何成果我依然擁有美好的生活	so , even if my physics research hadn't done anything , i'd still have a good life .
我試著在風景優美的地方居住	i'm trying to live in wonderful places .
過去十年我大部分時間都住在毛伊島一個超級漂亮的地方	for most of the past 10 years , i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .
現在我父母最大的謎團是我是怎樣在沒有一個全職工作的情況下活下來的	now , the biggest mystery in my parents was how i managed to survive all this time without fulltime career .
我要告訴你們這個秘密	i'm going to tell you the secret .
這是我在毛伊島上的家庭辦公室的照片	this is a picture of my home office on maui .
你們可能注意到這些照片似曾相似但背景稍有不同	you'll notice that these photos were similar , but the context is slightly different .
因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室	because this was my home and office in maui .
我選擇了一種不同尋常的生活	i chose a different kind of life .
不擔心房租讓我把時間花在喜歡做的事情上	and i don't worry about rent , so i spent my time doing what i love .
流浪的生活方式有時會很艱難也正因此我才能可生活在美麗的地方維持我所喜歡的平衡的生活	living a nomadic existence can be hard at times , and because of that , i'm able to live in a beautiful place and keep a balanced life that i'm so interested in .
我可以花大量的時間在超級聰明的珊瑚上	i could spend a lot of time on hyperintelligent corals .
同時我也很樂意和超級聰明的人打交道	and i'm also very happy to talk to hyperintelligent people .
很高興能被邀請到這兒演講	it's great to be invited here to give a talk .
我想我只懂了百分之二的部分 , 但是我絕對喜歡它 。 所以我想獻一下醜 。	i think i knew only two percent of it , but i absolutely liked it , so i wanted to advocate ugly .
你的萬物理論...我喜歡稱之為珊瑚理論	your theory of everything i like to call coral theory .
好吧 , 它讓人們興奮的原因是如果你是對的 , 那就把重力和量子理論結合了起來 。	well , it makes people excited because if you're right , it combines gravity and quantum theory .
所以你是不是說我們應該瞭解在宇宙中那些最微小的事物有可能就是e8模型 ?	so are you saying that we should understand that the tiniest things in the universe could be e8 ?
我是說 , 你心裡是不是有一個最小的尺寸 , 還是.... ?	i mean , does it have the smallest size in your mind , or is it . . .
嗯 , 剛剛給你們看得圖案就是我們所知的基本粒子物理 , 而且它已經是一個很漂亮的圖案了 。	well , the pattern i showed you is what we know about elementary particle physics , and it's already a beautiful pattern .
那個就是我所說的我們很確信的地方 。	that's what i said we know for sure .
而這個形狀和e8有著明顯的相似處 , 在剩下的圖片中幾乎和e8合為一體 。	and this shape has remarkable similarities with e8 in the rest of the picture .
我給你們看得這些點狀圖案實際上代表著高維物體的對稱性 , 這些圖案在我們生活的時空中 , 蜷曲 , 移動和舞蹈 。	i'm showing you these patterns of points actually represent symmetries of highdimensional objects that curl up and move and dance in the spacetime that we live .
這就解釋了所有的我們所看見的基本粒子 。	that explains all the elementary particles that we see .
克里斯:但是就我的理解 , 弦理論家會在更小的弦震動裡解釋電子--我知道你不喜歡弦理論 。	ca: but i understand that string theorists explain electrons in much smaller string vibrations i know you don't like string theory .
但我們該怎樣理解在e8模型中的電子 ?	but how can we understand the electrons in the e8 model ?
加勒特:不 , 它將會是這個e8型狀對稱性的一部分 。	gc: no , it's going to be part of this symmetry of this e8 shape .
所以實際上 , 當這個形狀在時空中游走 , 它會扭曲 。 而它扭曲的方向就是我們所看到的粒子 。 所以就是--e8形狀的大小 , 是怎麼樣和電子相聯絡的呢 ?	so in fact , as this shape is swimming around in spacetime , it's distorting , and it's distorting the direction of the particles that we see . so it's e8 shapes , how are they connected to the electron ?
我自己有些想象不出來 。	i have some imaginations myself .
它會大些還是小些 ?	is it bigger or smaller ?
嗯 , 就我們所知電子是點粒子 , 所以這個會讓我們看到最小的尺寸 。	well , as far as we can tell , electrons are particles , so this is what gives us the smallest scale .
所以在量子場論中 , 這些東西的解釋方式是所有的可能性都在同時展開發展 。	so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is that all of the possibilities are expanding and developing at the same time .
這也是我為什麼拿珊瑚作類比 。	and that's why i compare them to coral analogies .
因為這樣 , e8的進入方式是一個可以連線時空中每一點的形狀 。	because of this , the way e8 comes in is it's a shape that's linked in spacetime .
還有 , 想我所說的 , 形狀在經過這個曲線的表面時它的扭曲的方式和其的扭曲方向是基本粒子它們自己 。	and as i said , the shape twists the way it twists as it passes the surface of the curve and its distortion direction is the elementary particles themselves .
所以根據量子場論 , 它們自己把放大到和點一樣 , 然後相互作用 。	so , according to quantum field theory , they amplify it exactly like points and interact with each other .
我不知道我能不能解釋得更加清楚了 。	i don't know if i'm going to make that clearer .

它已經激起了我們的興趣 。 我確定我想了解的更多 。	it's been inspired by our interest . i'm sure i want to know a lot more .
太感謝你的光臨了 。 你的演說太吸引人了 。	thank you so much for coming . your talk is so fascinating .
研究黑猩猩的傳奇人物珍•古道爾講述有關tacare計劃以及她別的社群計劃 , 藉助這些計劃 , 在日益繁榮的非洲城鎮 , 人與瀕危動物可以和睦相處 。	studying the legends of chimpanzees , jane guur , talked about the tacare plan and her community project , and by helping these programs , in in increasingly thriving african towns , endangered people and endangered animals can meet .

我今晚的演講想從澤雷•阿蘭希格昨天留下的話題開始	what i'd like to talk to you about this evening is what i've been talking about with zerey alan higger did last night .
他談的是這個令人驚異的靈長類幼仔 , 叫selam , 三歲大	he was talking about this amazing primate child , selam , threeyearold .

已故古生物學家路易斯•李奇是他把我引上研究黑猩猩之路的	the late biologist louis leech , he introduced me to chimpanzees' path .
回顧過去 , 這條路實在不同尋常	when you look back on the road , it's quite an extraordinary path .
現在看來比較普通可他的論據是 , 因為他曾尋找在非洲的早期人類化石遺蹟	now it seems more average , but his argument is that he's searching for the early human fossil miracles in africa .
這些化石上 , 從附屬肌肉的形狀上 , 對於那些早期人類的模樣像什麼都能給研究者很多啟示從由他們身邊發現的原始工具上可以看出一些關於他們生活方式的端倪	these fossils , from the shape of a subordinate muscle , have a lot of revelations about what those early human appearances might look like in the raw tools around them .
但他們的行為表現是什麼樣的 ? 這是他想知道的	but what did they do ? well , he wanted to know .
當然 , 行為沒有在化石裡體現	of course , behavior doesn't embody that in the fossils .
他辨稱如果我們發現當代人類在行為模式上與和其最相近的物種巨猿相似或者相同那麼或許這些行為在大概七百萬年前在似猿似人的祖先身上存在過	he recognized that if we discovered that modern humans have been remarkably similar to their most similar ape patterns , then maybe these behaviors existed in the ancestors of similar australopithecines about seven million years ago .
因此 , 也許我們身上的那些行為特徵是從遠古時代傳下來的	so maybe those characteristics of our bodies are inherited from the distant past .
噢 , 如果你看一下現在講人類進化的書就會常常發現 , 人們是基於黑猩猩的行為表現來思考早期人類可能的行為方式	oh , if you look at the books that are talking about human evolution right now , it's often discovered that people are acting based on the behavior of chimpanzees to think about how early humans might behave .
與別的存活動物相比 , 他們更像我們這一點我在這次ted會議中聽到過	they're more like us here at the ted conference .
所以我今天要講的就是黑猩猩是在其行為方式的與人類的相似點	so what i'm going to talk about today is that the chimpanzees are very similar to the way they behave .
每個黑猩猩都有他/她自己的個性	every chimpanzee has his personality or her own personality .
當然 , 我給他們起名字 。 他們能活60歲或者更長儘管我們覺得他們中的絕大多數在野生環境活不到60歲	of course , i gave them names , and they lived 60 years or longer , although we think that the vast majority of them lived under 60 .
這是wurzel猩猩 。 母猩猩在11或12歲時生第一個孩子	this is wurzelle . females have the first baby at the age of 11 or 12 .
之後每五年或每六年她只生一仔這麼長的童年期內小猩猩很有依賴性 , 需要照料晚上和媽媽一起睡 , 騎在她背上	and every five or six years , she only had a very , very long childhood , a very dependent chimpanzee , and she had to take care of her mother to sleep at night , riding on her back .
我們認為這麼長的童年期對黑猩猩很重要 , 這牽涉到學習 , 就像童年之於我們一樣	we think it's such a long childhood that it's important for chimpanzees , and it's learning as we are in childhood .
在各種不同形態動物的進化過程中由於大腦變得日益複雜我們發現 , 在一種個體的生命歷程中學習的作用日益重要	in the evolution of all sorts of different forms of animals , with the brain getting more complicated , we find that the function of learning in an individual's life process is increasingly important .
年紀小的黑猩猩花很長時間觀察它們的長輩做什麼	young chimpanzees spend a very long time watching what their elders do .
我們現在知道 , 他們能模仿所見的行為表現	we now know that they can mimic what they see .
我們認為正是由此從那些在非洲研究的所有不同黑猩猩種群身上看到的使用工具的不同行為這些行為是怎樣透過觀察、模仿和實踐從一代傳到另一代的所以 , 我們可以把這些使用工具的行為說成是原始文化	we think that it's the kind of behavior that we're seeing with tools that we see in different chimpanzee groups of people who studied in africa through observation , imitation and practice from generation to generation , so that we can describe the behavior of those tools as being primal culture .
黑猩猩沒有語言 , 我們以前提到過	chimpanzees don't have language ; we've talked about it before .
但他們確實有一整套非常豐富的姿態和動作其中許多與我們的很像 , 甚至一模一樣並且具有相同涵義黑猩猩打招呼時會擁抱	but they do have a very rich set of gestures and actions , many of which are very similar to us , even identical to us , and have the same connotation that a chimpanzee would hug .
他們也親吻、牽手、一個拍另一個的背	they also kissed , held hands , one on the back .
他們也虛張聲勢地恐嚇 , 或者仍石頭	they're also bluffing , terrifying , or rocks .
在黑猩猩的社會里 , 我們發現很多很多憐憫、示愛以及真正利他的例子	in chimpanzee society , we find a lot of compassion and love and true examples of it .
和我們一樣 , 不幸的是 , 他們也有天性中陰暗的一面	and unfortunately , they have the dark side of nature , unfortunately .
他們可以極度兇殘 , 甚至像一種原始戰爭	they can be radically brutal , even a sort of primitive war .
多數情況下 , 這些極具攻擊性的行為是直接針對相鄰社群中個體的	and in many cases , these highly aggressive behaviors target individuals directly at neighboring communities .
這些攻擊大多是為了爭奪地盤	most of those attacks were about territory .
我覺得 , 與別的生物相比黑猩猩更有助於我們認識到 , 人類和動物王國裡的其他成員終歸併無明顯界限	i think it's helpful to recognize the limitations of humans and the rest of the animal kingdom in comparison with other animals .
這種界限非常模糊 , 並且隨著我們更多的觀察會一直更加模糊下去	it's a very blurry boundary , and it's always blurry as we get more observations .
我1960年開始的研究一直持續到現在	the study that i started in 1960 is ongoing .
這些黑猩猩在野生環境過著複雜的社會生活最重要的是 , 他們幫助我們認識到 , 我們與形形色色的動物在地球上共處 , 我們是其中一部分不能與這些動物分割開來	these chimpanzees live in complex societies in the wild , and most importantly , they help to recognize that we have a lot of animals that are format on earth , and we are part of the animals that cannot be separated from them .
所以 , 發現黑猩猩和世界上其他眾多生物一樣失去聚居地 , 是很讓人難過的	so it's sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other organisms around the world , have lost their concentrations .
這只是一張從空中拍的照片你可以看到森林覆蓋的gombe高地	this is just a photograph from the sky , and you can see the forest covered in gmbe height .
16年前 , 我走遍整個地區意識到在公園之外 , 這片森林在1960年時沿著tanganyika湖東岸綿延不絕小巧的、面積只有30平方英里的gombe國家公園就坐落在這裡那時一個問題進入我腦海	16 years ago , i traveled all over the region and realized that outside the park , this forest went all the way down to lake tanganyika in the 1960s and went all the way down to the east coast of lake tanganyika and banked 30 square miles of gombe national park , and there was a question that came to my mind .
" 我們怎麼能進而去試圖拯救這些出了名的黑猩猩 , 而住在國家公園周圍的人卻在為生存而掙扎 ? "	" how can we get there to try to save these famous chimpanzees , and the people who live around the park are struggling with surviving ? "
那裡人口眾多 , 非單薄的土地所能承受	there's a lot of people there , not just thin lands .
隨著來自蒲隆地的難民湧入來自剛果的人跨湖過來 , 住在那裡的人數增加著	and as refugees from burundi flooded the congolese crossed the lake , and there was an increase in number of people living .
那些人非常窮無力從別的地方買吃的	they're very , very poor people being bought from other places .
一個計劃由此產生 , 我們稱之為 " 關愛 "	and this is what we call a love project .
它用整體化的方式來改善住在湖周圍村子裡的人的生活	it improves the lives of people living in these villages around the surrounding area .
剛開始是小規模的 , 有12個村子 。 現在是24個	it started small , it had 12 villages . it's 24 now .
這裡沒有時間去深入介紹 , 不過該計劃包括象林木苗圃等事情 , 以及適於在山上這片目前嚴重剝蝕幾近沙漠的土地上耕種的方法	there's no time to go into this , but it involves things like forests , raised beds , and it's appropriate on mountains , and there's a very severe way to tillage the deserts .
控制、防止土地侵蝕的方法	it prevents control , it prevents land erosion .
收回過度使用的農田的方法以便兩年內這些農田可以重新有收成	overused farms were recycled for two years , and farms were recycled and recycled .
幫助村民從井裡取得淡水	help the villagers get fresh water from wells .
或許建一些校舍	maybe we can build some schoolrooms .
我認為最重要的是與小規模群體婦女合作給她們提供微型信用貸款的機會	i think most importantly , working with smallscale groups of women , offering them the opportunity to provide microcredit loans .
全世界的情況一樣 , 在所有貸款中我們收回了大約95%	and the same is true in all loans around the world , about 95 percent of all loans .
使婦女能夠受教育後工作給女孩子提供獎學金 , 以便讓她們完成中學學業很清楚 , 世界各地婦女的教育程度提高了 , 家庭人口數目就會下降	and that empowered women to have scholarships when they're educated so that they can finish middle school , and very clearly , women's education levels around the world are going to go down .
我們提供計劃生育和艾滋病及其病毒方面的資訊	we're providing plans for reproductive and hiv and viral information .
這項計劃實施之後自然保護方面發生了一些事情	and then something happened in the nature of this project .
自然保護方面發生的事情是 , 住在這24個村子裡的農民並沒有把我們看成是跑來研究整個一夥兒猴子的一夥兒白人順便說一下 , 現在很多工作人員是坦尚尼亞人而當我們開始 " 關愛 " 計劃時進入村子的是一個坦尚尼亞小組	what's happening with protection is that the farmers in these 24 villages , by the way , haven't looked at us as a part of a monkey and looked at the white guys of the monkey , by the way , are tanzanians , and when we started " fannisco , " the villages , they were the tanzanian group .
和村民交談的是一個坦尚尼亞小組詢問村民對什麼感興趣	talking to the villagers was a tanzanian group , asking what the villagers were interested in .
他們對自然保護感興趣嗎 ? 一點也不	are they interested in nature ? not at all .
他們對健康感興趣 , 他們對教育感興趣	they're interested in health , they're interested in education .
隨著時間推移 , 隨著他們境況開始改善他們開始不斷理解更多有關自然保護的必要性	and as time went on , as their circumstances began to improve , they began to understand the necessity of conservation .
他們開始理解當山上較高位置的數被砍光以後可怕的土地侵蝕和泥流就來了	they began to understand that when the higher numbers on the mountain were cut down , an awful lot of erosion and mud showed up .
現在 , 我們正在開發所說的大gombe生態系統	now we're developing what we call the gmbe ecosystem .
這是一片國家公園以外的地區綿延包括了所有這些各種各樣剝蝕了的土地	this is an area outside the national park that includes all these different kinds of erosion of land .
由於這些村子生活標準高一些他們實際上同意把他們土地的10-20%放到高地一側以便當樹長回來時黑猩猩會再次擁有綠色走廊它們可以藉此穿行以便這是他們基因繁殖所必需的與國家公園外其它殘餘群體互動	because of the standards of living in these villages , they actually agreed to put 10 to 20 percent of their land on the highland so that when the chimps would come back , they'd have green corridors again , so that they could wear all their gene breeding , so that they'd have to interact with all the rest of the population outside the national park .
所以 " 關愛 " 計劃成功了	so it's been successful in planning for love .
我們在非洲其它地區複製這項計劃在其它面臨極端人口壓力的荒野之地	we're replicating it in other parts of africa , in other parts of the world , in the wilderness of extreme population pressure .
但是 , 就像我們在ted開始的所有這幾天一直討論的非洲的問題是主要問題	but , like all of the problems that we've been talking about at ted these days , africa is a major problem .
那裡非常貧窮	it's a very poor place .
有大量的人生活在不那麼肥沃的土地上尤其當你把樹砍倒使得土壤裸露 , 任風侵蝕同時處於絕望的人砍倒越來越多的樹以便為他們自己和家人努力培育糧食這樣會發生什麼 ? 有些東西會開始犧牲讓步	the vast majority of people live on less fertile land , especially when you cut down trees and you erode the soil , and you get the wind eclipse , and the people in despair are losing more and more trees so that they can feed themselves and their families so that something can start sacrificing .
還有別的問題不僅在非洲而且是其它所有發展中世界 , 甚至是地球上所有地方我們在對我們的地球做什麼呢 ?	the other question is not just in africa , but all the other developing world , even everywhere on the planet , what are we doing to our planet ?
著名科學家 , e.o.威爾遜說過 , 如果地球上每個人的生活標準都達到歐美平均水平我們就再需要三個地球	the famous scientist , e . o . wilson , said that if every person on the planet at their standard of living , on average , we'd need three more planets .
今天他們說是四個 。 可我們沒那些個 , 我們只有一個	today they say four . we don't have one . we only have one .
發生了什麼 ? 我是說 , 這裡的問題是 , 我們在這裡或許可稱為地球上有史以來最有智慧的生命有著非凡的大腦能夠運用這些ted會議上闡述備至的這些技術但我們卻在毀壞著這個惟一的家園	what's happening ? i mean , the question here is , we may be able to call it the most intelligent life on earth , the most intelligent beings that have ever been on this earth , with extraordinary brains that have been able to use these ted conferences to illustrate what's being said , but we are destroying this unique home
全球各地的原住民在做重要決定前都會坐到一起 , 然後問 " 這決定如何影響我們接下來的七代人 ? "	natives all over the world will sit together before important decisions , and will say , " how does this determine affect the next seven generations ? "
今天 , 重要決定我這裡不特別談非洲而是發達世界牽涉幾百萬美元以及以及幾百萬人的重要決定卻只是問 " 這會如何影響下次股東大會 ? "	today , critical decisions i'm not talking about africa , i'm talking about the world in terms of the millions of dollars that are involved and the millions of people just asking , " how does it impact the next shareholder meeting ? "
這些決定卻影響非洲	these decisions affect africa .
當我開始遊歷非洲談論黑猩猩面臨的問題及其日益消逝的森林我愈來愈意識到如此之多的非洲問題是如何與以前的殖民開發有關的	as i started to travel and talk about issues facing chimpanzees and their growing forests , i started to realize how so many africans have been associated with former colonial development .
因此我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 在歐洲演講在美國演講 , 去亞洲	so i started traveling beyond africa , speaking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .
每一地都有這些糟糕的問題	and everywhere has these terrible problems .
你知道我說的是什麼問題 , 這包括汙染問題	you know what i'm talking about , including pollution .
我們呼吸的空氣經常毒害我們	the air that we breathe constantly poisons us .
泥土毒害我們的食物	mud poisoning our food .
水水也許是本世紀我們要面對的最要緊問題之一每一地 , 水都被農業、工業、家用化學制品所汙染全世界都還在噴這些製品似乎沒辦法從過去的經驗獲利	water is perhaps one of the most troubling problems we have to confront in this century , and every single place is contaminated by agriculture and industry and home chemicals all over the world , and it seems like it's not benefiting from the past .
紅樹被砍倒海嘯等影響日益加重	red trees are being chopped down , tsunamis are getting better , etc .
我們談過土壤侵蝕	we talked about soil erosion .
我們不計後果地燒過化石燃料連同其它所謂溫室氣體導致了氣候變化	we've all been burning fossil fuels in regular consequences , along with other known as greenhouse gasses , causing
終於 , 全世界的人都開始相信有什麼事發生了 , 我們的氣候不對勁兒了	and finally , people all over the world are believing that something happened , our climate wasn't right .
全球氣候互相牽連	the global climate is attached .
最受不利影響的是窮人	the worst impacts are the poor .
已經受影響的是非洲	it's african already affected .
在次撒哈拉非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱非常嚴重	in many parts of subsaharan africa , droughts are serious .
雨終於下起來時 , 又常常導致洪水及更多的不幸 , 貧窮、飢餓和疾病週而復始	when the rains come down , it often leads to flooding and a lot of misfortune , poverty , hunger and disease .
還有很多人住在土地供養不起的地區太窮 , 買不起食物因為全部土地都剝蝕了 , 所以也沒法離開	and there's also a lot of people living in land that's too poor to buy food , because it's stripped all the land , and they can't leave .
於是有了沙漠化一點點漫延 , 漫延 , 漫延同時最後的樹也被砍倒	so you have desertification a little bit , a little bit of a delay , a little bit of a delay , and then at the same time , the last trees are being cut down .
這種事情不光在非洲遍佈全球	and it's not just that this is happening all over the world .
所以我不覺得奇怪當我在世界各地旅行時碰到那麼多年輕人 , 他們看上去失去了希望	so i don't think it's surprising that when i travel around the world and i meet so many young people , they seem to have lost hope .
我們似乎已經失去了智慧 , 那種屬於原住民的智慧	we seem to have lost wisdom , the indigenous wisdom of the indigenous people .
我想問 , 這是為什麼 ?	i wanted to ask , why is that ?
你們覺得在這異常聰明的大腦ted技術作為例證的那種大腦和人的心臟之間會有某種隔絕嗎 ? 用非科學的術語來談談根據愛和同情 。 有隔絕嗎 ?	do you think there's some kind of a separation between the brain and the heart of the brain in an unscientific term , according to love and compassion ?
這些年輕人 , 當我和他們講話時基本上他們要麼情緒低落 , 要麼無動於衷或者痛苦、憤怒他們或多或少說的是同一件事情 " 我們這麼感覺是因為我們覺得你們損害了我們的未來 , 並且我們對此無能為力 。 "	these young people , when i talk to them , basically they're either emotionally low , or they're obsessed or painful or angry , and they're all talking more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel like you've broken our future , and we can't help . "
我們確實已經毀壞了他們的未來	we have destroyed their future .
我有三個小孫子 , 每次看著他們我就想 , 從我像他們那麼大以來 , 我們是如何損害這個美麗的地球的我感覺到這種絕望	i have three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them , i wonder how we've harmed this beautiful earth since i was so big as them , i feel this despair .
我們由此開展這項我們稱之為 " 根與芽 " 的計劃恰好始於這裡 , 坦尚尼亞現在已經傳播到世界上97個國家	and we started this project that we're calling roots and shoots , and it just started out here , tanzania has now spread to 97 countries in the world .
專案的名字是具有象徵意義的根造就堅實的基礎	the name of the project is the symbolic root of meaning .
芽看上去細小 , 在陽光照耀下卻可穿破磚牆	germs look small , but under sunlight , they can break through a brick wall .
磚可以看成是我們給地球造成的環境的和社會的問題這是希望的訊息	blocks can see the environmental and social problems that we have created on the planet , and that's the message of hope .
世界各地成千上萬的年輕人可以取得突破 , 為了所有生物 , 讓這個世界更美好	hundreds of thousands of young people around the world have access to breakthroughs for all living things to make the world a better place .
" 根與芽 " 的最重要訊息每一天 , 我們每一個人都在改變世界	the most important message of roots and shoots is that every single day , each and every one of us is changing the world .
我們有一個選擇這屋子裡我們每一個人我們都有一個選擇 , 關於我們想做些什麼來改變世界	we have a choice in this room , and each and every one of us , we have a choice about what we want to do to change the world .
很窮的人沒有選擇我們要改變這些事以便窮人也有選擇	very poor people don't choose to change those things , so the poor have a choice .
" 根與芽 " 小組都選三個方案	the roots and shoots group selected three schemes .
取決於成員年齡 , 所在國家在城市還是鄉下 , 來選不同的方案	it depends on membership , on whether or not the country is urban or rural , to choose different programs .
基本上 , 我們現在的計劃從學前一直到大學愈來愈多的成人開始建立他們自己的 " 根與芽 " 小組	basically , what we're planning to do is , we've gone from school to college , and more adults are starting to build their own group of roots and shoots .
每個小組在彼此之間選擇三種不同的方案 , 來創造更加美好的世界承認所有這些不同問題是互相聯絡彼此影響的	each group chose each other three different programs to create a better world recognition that all of these different issues were contact with one another .
因此他們的方案之一將會幫助他們自己的人類社群	so one of their solutions will be to help their own human communities .
然後 , 如果他們能幹 , 他們可以籌集資金幫助世界上其它地區的社群	and then , if they can do that , they can raise funds to help communities in other parts of the world .
他們的方案之一將會幫助動物不光是野生動物也包括家養動物	one of their solutions will be to help the animals , not just in wildlife , but including families .
他們的方案之一將會幫助我們共處的環境	one of their solutions will be to help us all live in an environment .
交織在所有這些方案中的訊息是學著與我們自己、家庭、社群和諧相處 , 包括國家之間 , 不同文化之間不同宗教信仰之間 , 以及我們和自然世界之間	the message of woven into all of these programs is to learn to harmonize ourselves , families , communities , including countries , between different religious beliefs , and between us and the natural world .
我們需要自然世界我們不能繼續象現在這樣破壞世界了	we need the natural world , and we can't continue to do that anymore .
我們只有一個地球	we only have one planet .
就在非洲這裡 , 僅僅選出一個或兩個 " 根與芽 " 小組正在實施的方案只要一個或兩個方案在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果、布拉扎維、獅子山、喀麥隆以及別的團體 。 就象我說的 , 遍佈世界97個國家	right here in africa , the mere elect of just one or two roots and shoots is implementing one or two programs in tanzania , uganda , kenya , south africa , congo , brave , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups , like i said , in 97 countries .
當然 , 他們種樹 , 他們種有機蔬菜	of course , they plant trees , they grow organic vegetables .
他們在難民營養小雞賣雞蛋得些微薄收入或只是把雞蛋給家人吃並覺得自豪和獲得權力因為他們自己種植蔬菜養殖小雞就不再無助 , 不再依賴他人	they sell chicken eggs at refugee nutritional chickens , either they feed their families and feel pride and receive power , because they grow their own vegetables and they grow their own chickens without help , no longer depend on others .
這個方案在烏干達實施了給予前童軍一些心理上的幫助	this program implemented a psychological help for the former scouts in uganda .
實施這些方案讓他們重塑自我	implementing these programs allows them to reinvent themselves .
再一次 , 他們成為社會上的有用一員	and once again , they're useful in society .
我們也在監獄實施該計劃	we've also implemented it in prison .
所以現在沒時間實施更多的 " 根與芽 " 計劃	so there's no time to do more roots and shoots .
哦 , 他們也致力於艾滋病及其病毒方面的工作	oh , they're also working on hiv and its viruses .
那是 " 根與芽 " 計劃非常重要的組成部分由大孩子跟小孩子談話	it's a very important component of the roots and shoots , and it's all about the grown kids talking to kids .

藝術家戴安娜•科恩分享關於塑膠汙染對大海和我們日常生活嚴重影響的事實和一些想法 , 幫助大家來擺脫塑膠包圍圈 。	the artist diana cohen shared the fact that plastic pollution has severe effects on the sea and on our daily lives , helping people out of plastic wrappers .
consumerism , globalissues , green , missionblue , oceans , plastic	" consumerism , " and the global global isis sues , green , mission blue , the oceans , the plastics .
戴安娜•科恩diannacohen:關於塑膠汙染的嚴峻事實	diana cohen: the harsh truth about plastic pollution .
我是個視覺藝術家 , 也是塑膠汙染聯盟的創始人之一 。	i'm a visual artist and one of the founders of the plastic pollution coalition .
過去20年 , 我一直參與塑膠包的工作 , 我藝術創作的原材料是裁製和縫合塑膠 。	for the last 20 years , i've been involved in plastic packets , and my artistic raw material is tailoring and sewing plastic .
讓塑膠變為平面和立體型藝術 , 雕塑和藝術裝置 。	let's make plastics a flat and threedimensional art , sculpture and art installation .
在與塑膠打交道的八年之後 , 我的一些作品開始開裂碎成許多小塑膠塊 。	after eight years of dealing with plastic , some of my work began to split into little plastic blobs .
我想 , " 好極了 。	and i thought , " great .
塑膠就像我們人類一樣短命 。 "	plastics are as short as us humans . "
我自學進一步深入瞭解塑膠 , 我的確瞭解到塑膠是個壞材料 。	i learned more about plastics myself , and i did realize that plastic was a bad material .
塑膠碎成許多小塊 , 但它還是塑膠 , 這很糟糕 。	plastics are broken up into lots of little bits , but it's still plastic , which is awful .
我們發現有很多塑膠漂浮於大海 。	we found a lot of plastic floating in the ocean .
然而在過去的幾年 , 我知道太平洋垃圾環流和垃圾漩渦 。	but for the last several years , i've known about pacific garbage patch and trash gyre .
我第一反應--我想這也是多數人的第一反應 , 知道這之後-- " 喔 , 我的上帝 !	my first response and i think that's the first response to a majority , to know , " oh , my god !
我們要去那裡並清理這些塑膠 。 "	we're going to go there and clean up the plastics . "
所以我提議一隻貨船 , 兩隻退役拖網漁船 , 一臺起重機 , 一臺削片機和一臺冷壓機出海 。	so i proposed a container , two retired trawlers , a crane , a slash machine and a cold presser exiting the sea .
我計劃是航行到垃圾環流帶 , 提高對於此汙染的高度重視 , 開始回收塑膠 , 切割它變成小片 , 然後冷壓變成塑膠塊 , 它可能被用來作為欠發達社群的建築材料 。	my plan was to voyage to a garbage dumpster zone , raising a high value for this pollution and recycled plastic , cut it into small plastic and compressed into plastic , and it might be used as a material to encounter a community .
我同那些曾去過垃圾環流帶的人們談過 , 他們也曾研究過塑膠汙染對海洋環境的汙染 , 交談之後 , 我開始意識到海上清理塑膠相比起全球每天產生塑膠的生產量就如大海撈針一樣 , 我必須回過頭想想 , 要展望更大的藍圖 。	i've spoken with people who've been to the garbage dumpsters , and they've also studied plastic pollution in the marine environment , and after that , i've become aware of the ocean cleaning plastics just like needles all over the world , and i've got to go back and think of the bigger blueprints to look at .
真正的解決辦法就是:我們需要在源頭找到解決方法 。	the real solution is that we need to find solutions at the source .
我們需要切斷一次性使用塑膠和一次性塑膠的源頭 , 使得它們在全球範圍內每天不會再進入大海 。	we need to cut the sources of plastic and oneoff plastics so that they don't go into the ocean every day on a global scale .
看看這個 , 我也知道我非常生氣 。	look at this , and i know i'm angry .
我並不只關心你也可能想象到的在太平洋中部我們現在所知的 , 權威資料是 , 11個垃圾塑膠環流帶 , 遍及世界五大海洋 。	and i'm not just concerned about what you might think of in the middle of the pacific , but the authority data is , 11 garbage zones all over the world and five oceans .
我不僅僅是關心塑膠環流帶 , 也包括超市的塑膠包圍圈 。	i'm not just concerned about the plastic rings , but also the plastic rings in the supermarket .
我要去超市 , 所有事物都是塑膠包裝 。	i'm going to the supermarket and everything's packaging .
所有飲料都是塑膠包裝 , 甚至健康的有機市場 。	all drinks are plastic packaging and even healthy organic markets .
我也關注在冰箱的塑膠 , 還有塑膠以及濾取塑膠的毒素被我們吃下和吸收到我們身體裡 。	i'm also concerned about the plastics in the refrigerator , and the toxins in the plastic and the filter plastic that we eat and absorb .
我和其他的一群人們都關注這個塑膠汙染問題 , 組建了塑膠汙染聯盟 。	i and a whole bunch of other people focused on this plastic pollution problem and formed the plastic pollution coalition .
我們為解決這問題開始許多活動 , 它們中的一些是非常簡單的 。	we started a lot of activities to solve this problem , and some of them are very simple .
其中一個是:在大海 , 我們發現百分80到百分90海洋廢棄物是塑膠 , 然後我們為什麼不稱其為:	one of them was , in the ocean , we found that 80 to 90 percent of marine waste is plastic , and why don't we call it plastic ?
再迴圈 。 關於可持續和再迴圈的環保想法的書籍都是類似的觀點 。	again , books about sustainable and recycled environmental ideas have similar ideas .
大家扔東西到垃圾桶裡 , 但是從來沒有再想過此事 。	people were throwing things in trash cans , but never thought about it again .
現實是什麼呢 ?	what is reality ?
在美國 , 塑膠垃圾回收率少於百分之七 。	in the u . s . , plastic waste is less than seven percent .
大家想實際看看 , 特別當塑膠變成塑膠瓶 , 絕大多數塑膠瓶僅被降級回收 , 或者焚燒 , 或運到中國 。	people actually think that plastic bottles in particular become plastic bottles , most plastic bottles are degraded or incinerated or shipped to china .
當一個塑膠瓶可以被重製成一個塑膠瓶 , 或者重被使用時 , 正是被降級回收 , 使得塑膠瓶被製成小塑膠體 , 使得一個塑膠瓶不再被製成塑膠瓶回收利用 。	when a plastic bottle can be rebuilt to a plastic bottle or reused , it's been degraded to recycle its plastic bottle as tiny plastic bottle and make a plastic bottle no longer recycles its bottle .
對我們而言 , 這是個重大問題 。	it's a huge problem for us .
我們關注 , 並讓人們思考的另一件事是我們在原本3個r原則前 , reduce、reuse、recycle , 加了第四個r原則 , 它就是拒絕使用 。	the other thing we're looking at and letting people think about is that we reduce , reuse , recycle , and recycle , before our triple principle .
無論何時 , 拒絕使用一次性使用塑膠和即丟塑膠 。	whenever you refuse to use onetime plastic and disposable plastic .
有替代品的使用 。 其中一些是非常老套 。	there are alternative uses . some of them are very oldfashioned .
我自己現在收集這些很酷的耐熱玻璃容器 , 使用這些而替換高興派和特百惠派塑膠容器來儲存食物 。	i myself am now collecting these cool , heatedrous glass vessels that use these instead of amgent and extractive plastic vessels to store food .
我知道我這樣做有利於我自己和我的家庭 。	i knew i was doing it for myself and my family .
我們選擇使用不鏽鋼瓶和玻璃瓶是很容易的 , 你如果要出門 , 記得帶不鏽鋼瓶 , 讓它灌滿水 , 或者濾過水 , 而不要購買塑膠瓶裝水 。	it's easy to choose the stainless steel bottle and glass bottles if you want to get out , to remember that the stainless steel bottle is filled with water , or you filter it over the water , rather than buying plastic bottles of water .
我猜我想要告訴大家的是我知道你們大家關於此塑膠汙染知道得很多漂在大海上的塑膠是個嚴重的問題 , 但這是我們做為消費者自身產生的問題 , 我們也能自身解決這問題 。	i guess what i'd like to suggest to you is that i know that you guys know about this plastic pollution that a lot of plastic in the ocean is a serious problem , but it's a problem that we're generating as consumers , and we can solve it ourselves .
我們透過提高這問題的意識 , 教導人們選擇可替換性產品 , 能夠解決這問題 。	and by raising the consciousness of the problem , we have taught that people choosing alternative products could solve the problem .
所以無論何時 , 請選擇使用可替換性產品 , 拒絕使用一次性使用塑膠和即丟塑膠 。	so whenever you're choosing an alternative product , you refuse to use onetime plastic and disposable plastic .
我們可以切斷源頭 , 阻止這塑膠汙染到我們的海洋裡 , 透過如上4r行動 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的家園 , 拯救我們自己 。	we can cut sources and prevent this plastic pollution into our oceans by 4r movements to save our oceans and save ourselves from our homes .

現在 , 我將這個裝置展示給大家 。 這是我們至今最成功的版本 , 仍然在不斷改進 。	now , i'll show you this device , and this is the most successful version of our time , and it's still improving .

我佩戴著一個相機 , 就是一個簡單的網路攝像頭 , 一個便攜的用電池供電的投影儀和一個小鏡子 。	i'm wearing a camera , a simple webcam , a portable battery projector and a tiny mirror .
這些元件跟我口袋中的手機進行通訊 , 手機作為一個通訊和計算的裝置 。	these elements communicate with my cell phone in my pocket as a communication and computational device .
畫面中 , 是我的天才學生pranavmistry , 他設計並製造了這整套系統 。	this is my genius student pranavmistry , who's designed and created this entire system .

但當你想到你的朋友是長期的冒險活動時 , 因此 , 它是你為增加壽命和讓生命生機勃勃能夠做的最重要的事情謝謝	but when you think about your friends , it's longterm adventures , and therefore , it's the most important thing that you do to increase your lifespan and make life erectile .
能導電的墨水、一<unk>開關就由透明變不透明的窗戶、能播放音樂的果凍--這些東西確實存在 。 catarinamota說:現在是時候嘗試他們了 。 mota將帶領我們認識這些新穎和神奇的材料 , 她說 , 弄清楚這些材料的神奇之處的最好方式就是用它們來做實驗 , 不斷嘗試並樂在其中 。	and it's a picture of ink that conducts electricity , and it turns out , of transparency windows , frozen music those things actually exist . catarina mota says they're going to do it now . mota will lead us to understand these novelty and magic materials , and she said , the best way to do it is to try and play and experiment with these materials .
creativity , design , technology	so let's make sure that's what's going to happen to you .
catarinamota:玩轉智慧材料	catarina mota: to play with smart materials .
我有一位葡萄牙朋友 , 其祖父用一輛腳踏車和一臺洗衣機改裝成一輛汽車供家人乘用 。	i have a friend of portuguese whose grandfather converted to a bicycle and a washing machine into an automobile for his family .
他這樣做 , 一是因為他買不起車 , 但更重要的是因為他知道如何改裝汽車 。	he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but more importantly because he knew how to convert a car .
曾經 , 我們都懂得一些機械的工作原理 , 也知道它們是怎麼製造出來的 , 所以我們能夠自己製作和維修它們.或者至少基於我們的瞭解作出明智的購買決定 。	we've all understood the principles of mechanical work and how they're made , so we can make and repair them ourselves , or at least we can make decisions about wise purchases .
但我們很多這些diy的實用性技能在20世紀的下半葉就流失了 。	but many of these diy practical skills were lost in the second half of the 20th century .
但是現在 , 製作者社群和開放資源模式正在把這些物品的工作原理和製造材料的知識帶回到我們的生活中 。 而且我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個層面 , 也就是了解構成這些物品的元件 。	but now , the maker community and open source model are taking the principles of these things and the knowledge of the materials to our lives , and i'm convinced that we need to bring them to the next level , which is to understand the components of these objects .
我們很多人都知道 , 像紙和織物這樣的傳統材料是什麼做成的 , 以及它們是如何生產的 。	many of us know what traditional materials like paper and fabric are made of , and how they're made .
但是現在我們有了一些令人驚歎的未來複合材料-如可以變形的塑膠、可以導電的油漆、可以變色的顏料和可以發光的織物 。	but now we have some remarkable future complexs like deformable plastic , conductive paint , colorchanging pigments and fabrics that can glow .
下面讓我們來看一些新材料 。	so let's look at some new materials .
這種導電墨水可讓我們 , 拋棄傳統的印刷電路板或電線的方法而直接用導電墨水來畫電路板 。	this conductive ink allows us to throw out traditional printing boards or wires and directly draw electrical boards with conductive ink .
比如我手裡拿著的這個小裝置 , 是我們用導電墨水做成一個觸控性的感測器 , 一旦接觸人的皮膚 , 這個小燈就會亮起 。	this little device that i'm holding in my hand is a controlled sensor that we're using conductive inks to make , and once we're exposed to the skin , it lights up .
導電墨水已經被藝術家們應用到創作中了 , 最新的進展表明我們很快就能把它應用在鐳射印表機和鐳射筆中.	the conductive ink was being applied to artists , and the most recent advanced suggests that we could soon be applied to a laser printer and a laser beam .
這是一張泡浸過無色光漫顆粒丙烯酸的紙.	this is a piece of paper that's bathed in colorless luminous particles .
只浸過普通丙烯酸的紙只在其邊緣周圍有漫光現象 , 而這張浸過無色光漫顆粒丙烯酸的紙 , 當我們開燈時漫光會照亮整張紙.	immersed only a regular acrylic only has vast phenomena around its edge , and this one immersed a highlighted , highlighted , luminous particles of alanine , lighting the entire piece of paper as we turned on the light .
就目前所知 , 這種材料已經被應用到室內設計和多點觸控系統兩個領域中了 。	and as we've seen , this material has been used in two areas of interior design and multitouch systems .
而熱變色顏料在特定的溫度下會改變顏色 。	and thermal pigment changes color at a particular temperature .
我先把這張東西放到一個電熱板上溫度設定比外界溫度稍高一點然後你可以看到發生了什麼.	i'm going to put this on a temperature board a hot slightly higher temperature than the outside world , and you can see what happens .
除了其它用途 , 這種材料主要用作嬰兒奶瓶的製造 。 它能告訴你什麼時候瓶裡的東西涼到可飲用的溫度 。	except for other things , the material is mostly used as makers of baby bottles , and it can tell you when something in your bottle is cool to drinkable temperature .
這些就是我們通常所說的 " 智慧材料 " 的幾個例子 。	these are just a few examples of what we usually call " smart materials . "
幾年內 , 它們將被應用到很多我們日常使用的物件和科技產品上 。	in a few years , they're going to be used for lots of objects and technology products that we use every day .
我們也許還不會有科幻小說向我們保證的飛行汽車 , 但是我們能擁有隨溫度變色的牆 , 可以捲起來的鍵盤 , 和一<unk>開關就變不透明的窗戶 。	we may not yet have science fiction flying cars that we guarantee , but we can have walls that are curled up with temperature , keyboards that are on the roll , that aren't opening windows that are opaque .
我是科班出身的社會科學家 , 為什麼今天我在這裡講智慧材料 ?	i'm a social scientist by the cochrane , and why am i here today talking about smart materials ?
首先 , 我是個製造者 。	first of all , i'm a maker .
我對於東西如何運轉和怎樣製作有好奇心 , 我也相信我們應該對我們這個世界的組成材料有更深的瞭解 , 並且現在 , 我們對於這些構成我們未來的高科技材料瞭解不多 。	i'm curious about how things work and how they work , and i'm convinced that we should have deeper understanding of the materials that make up our world , and right now , we don't know very much about these hightech materials that make us who we are .
要獲得少量的智慧材料是很難的 。	it's hard to get a small amount of smart material .
有關如何使用這些材料的資訊也很少 , 它們是如何製作的資訊就更加少得可憐 。	there's very little information about how you use these materials , and they're much less miserable information about how you make them .
目前 , 它們絕大多數都存在於貿易機密和專利中 , 只有大學和大公司才能得到 。	currently , they are mostly in secrets of trade secrets and patents , just for universities and large companies .
所以三年多以前 , 我和kirstyboyle發起了一個叫做openmaterials的專案 。	so three years ago , i launched a project called open materials called the kirstyboyle .
在那個網站上 , 我們和想要加入我們的任何人 , 分享實驗 , 釋出資訊 , 鼓勵其他人為此作出力所能及的貢獻 , 並且收集像研究論文和像我們一樣的製造者所製作的教程一類的資源 。	on that website , we're sharing experiments with anyone that wants to join us , release information , encourage others to make their contributions to this , and collect resources like research papers made by makers like ours .
我們希望把這一網站做成一個大規模的、集體生成的資料庫 , 蒐集用智慧材料diy的資訊 。	we wanted to take this website and create a largescale , collectively generated database and gather information about smart materials , diy .
但是我們為什麼要關心智慧材料是如何工作和它們是用什麼來製造的呢 ?	but why should we care about how intelligent materials work and how they're made from ?
首先 , 因為我們無法影響我們不理解的東西 , 我們不理解和不會用的東西還會反過來影響我們 。	first , because we can't influence things that we don't understand , we don't understand and don't use things to influence us .
我們使用的東西 , 我們穿的衣服 , 我們住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活質量上產生深遠的影響 。	the things we use , the clothes we use , the houses we live in have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .
所以如果我們將要生活在一個由智慧材料構成的世界中 , 我們就應該知道並瞭解它們 。	so if we're going to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .
第二 , 同樣重要地 , 創新總是來源於修補匠 。	secondly , just as importantly , innovation always comes from fixing the maker .
很多時候 , 是業餘愛好者而非專家 , 發明和改進了諸如山地車、半導體、個人電腦、甚至飛機 。	in many cases , hobbyists and not experts , inventions and improvements like mountain vehicles , semiconductors , personal computers , or airplanes .
材料科學的最大挑戰是它的複雜性 , 以及對昂貴的儀器的需求 。	one of the biggest challenges in material science is its complexity and the need for expensive equipment .
但事實並非總如此 。	but that's not always the case .
伊利諾伊大學的兩名科學家在他們發表一篇關於用更簡便的方法制作導電墨水的論文時就明白了這個道理 。	two scientists at the university of illinois published an article about conducting electricity inks in a more convenient way .
jordanbunker在這一實驗之前是一個沒有任何化學經驗的人 。 他讀了這篇論文後在他的工作間裡用現成的物質和工具重複了這個實驗 。	jordanbunker was a man who didn't have any chemical experience in this experiment , and he read the paper and repeated it in his own work .
他用了一個烤箱 , 而且他甚至在另一個科學家/製造者的教程的基礎上自制了旋渦混合器 。	he took a oven , and he even made himself a turbine hybrid mixer at the basis of another scientist/maker .
後來 , jordan在網上發表了他的實驗結果 , 包括所有他試過的沒成功的東西 , 這樣其他人可以學習然後複製這一實驗 。	and jordan published his experiments online , including all the unsuccessful things that he had tried so that others could learn and replicate this experiment .
所以jordan主要創新方式是拿一個在設施齊全的大學實驗室裡創造的實驗 , 然後在芝加哥的一個車庫裡用便宜材料和自制的工具來重複實驗 。	so jordan's main innovation is to take an experiment that was created in a university laboratory and repeat it in a garage in chicago using cheap materials and selfcontrolled tools .
在他發表的實驗結果基礎上 , 其他人可以接著做下去並且設計甚至更簡單的步驟和改進實驗 。	and based on the experimental results he published , others can then do this , and even simpler steps and advances .
我想分享的另外一個例子她專案的目標是在突出材料富有表現力的特質的同時專注於製造者的創造力和製造技巧 。	another example i want to share with you is that her project is focused on emerging quality of expertise and also focusing on the creativity and manufacturing skills of makers .
電子工具在教我們東西如何運轉這方面非常有力 , 但是它們設計中傳承下來的約束影響我們學習的方式 。	electronics are very powerful in teaching us how things work , but the disciplines that they have inherited in their design impact the way we learn .
所以hannah的方法 , 在另一方面 , 就是創制一系列的技術 , 來創造非常規的東西 , 透過教給我們材料本身的知識 , 把我們從事先設計好的約束中解放出來 。	so the hannah approach , on the other hand , is creating a series of techniques to create really normative things by teaching us the knowledge of the material itself to free us from predesigned constraints .
在hannah眾多令人欽佩的試驗中 , 這個是我的最愛之一 。	in hannah , this is one of my favorite trials .
[ " 會說話的紙 " ]我們在這裡看到的只不過是一張紙上面的銅帶連線著一個mp3播放器和一塊磁鐵 。	[ " paper of speech " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper that has a copper tape attached to it , an mp3 player and a magnet .
在麻省理工學院教授marcelocoelho研究的基礎上 , hannah使用各種材料創造了一系列紙質揚聲器 。 從普通的銅帶到導電的織物和墨水 ,	in mit , professor marce locoelho studied basically , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of materials from ordinary copper to fabric fabrics and inks that conduct electricity .
就像jordan和其他很多製造者一樣 , hannah發表了她的配方並且允許任何人來重複這些實驗 。	just like jordan and many other makers , hannah published her recipe and allowed anyone to repeat these experiments .
但是紙上電子是材料科學中最有前景的分支之一 , 因為它讓我們能創造出便宜又靈活的電子產品 。	but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science because it allows us to create cheap , flexible electronics .
所以hannah的手工作品 , 和她分享了她的發現這個事實 , 打開了一扇門 , 通向兼具美學和創新的一系列新的可能 。	so hannah's hand work was sharing her discovery of the truth , opening a door to a series of new possibilities for both aesthetic and innovation .
製造者的有趣之處在於我們創造是出於熱情和好奇 , 並且我們不害怕失敗 。	the funny thing about makers is that we create enthusiasm and curiosity , and we don't fear failure .
我們通常從非傳統的角度處理問題 , 並且 , 在這個過程中 , 最終發現其他方案或者更好的方法 。	we typically approach problems from an unconventional perspective , and in the process , we find other alternatives or better ways .
所以當更多的人願意用新材料做試驗的時候 , 更多的研究者就會願意分享他們的研究成果 ; 有更多的製造商分享他們的知識 , 我們就會有更好的機會來創造造福我們所有人的科技 。	so when more people are willing to experiment with new materials , more researchers will be willing to share their results ; more manufacturers will share their knowledge , and we'll have a better opportunity to create technologies for all of us .
我的感覺有一點像tednelson在70年代初期的感覺一樣 , 他寫道 , " 你們現在必需懂電腦 。 "	i feel a little bit like tednelson in the early '70s feeling , and he wrote , " you need to know computers now . "
那個時候 , 電腦是這些只有科學家關心的大型機 , 沒有人會夢想到放一臺在家裡 。	at the time , the computer was these large machines only scientists care about , and no one dreamed of placing a home .
所以我今天站在這裡說 " 你們現在必需懂智慧材料 " 有一點奇怪 。	so i stand here today and i say , " you need to understand your smart material " a little strange .
請記住對於新興科技擁有先發制人的知識是確保我們在對未來的創造中有發言權的最好方式 。	please keep in mind that the preemptive knowledge of emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the creation of the future .
當我們開車是 , 我們就坐進了一個玻璃氣泡中 , 鎖上門 , 踩下油門 , 依靠眼睛為我們自己導航 。 即使我們僅僅只能看見車前車後的幾輛車 。 但是假如汽車能互換關於位置、速度的資料 , 並運用預測模型來為每一位司機測算最安全的線路呢 ? 詹妮佛海麗構想了一個零車禍的世界 。	and as we drove it , we sat in a glass bubble , locked the door , stepped on the gas door and navigated ourselves , even though we could only see just a few cars behind the train , but what if cars could exchange data about location , speed , and use the prediction model to predict the safest course for each driver , jennifer hay , for example , conceive a world of zero accidents ?
詹妮弗海麗:汽車若能交流車禍或可避免	jennifer haley: vehicles can exchange or avoid .
讓我們來面對一樁事實吧開車是一件危險的事	let's face the fact that driving is a dangerous thing .
它是我們不願意去想的事物之一但事實上那些神像和平安符世界各地都有人把它們擺在儀表盤的上方這就無意中透露出一個我們都心知肚明的事實	it's one of the things that we don't want to think about , but in fact , the gods are peaceful and peaceful , everywhere around the world , and it reveals an inadvertent reality of what we all know .
車禍是死亡的主因尤其在美國16到19歲的美國人群中死亡的主因並且百分之七十五的車禍都與毒品和酒精無關	car accidents are the cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states , and 75 percent of those crashes are not drugs and alcohol .
沒人能給出確切答案但我記得我第一次出車禍	no one can give an exact answer , but i remember the first crash i had .
我當時還是個開車的新手 , 當時正在外面高速路上開著車 。 我突然看見我前面汽車的剎車燈亮了	i was a new car driving , and i was driving down the highway , and all of a sudden i saw the brake lights in front of me .
我當時想好吧他減速了那我也減速好了	and i thought , ok , he's slowing down . i'll slow down .
我踩了剎車	i step on the brakes .
但是我前面那個人並不是在減速	but the guy in front of me wasn't slowing down .
他停車了突然停車在高速路上突然停車	he stopped in the highway , and all of a sudden he had stopped .
速度從65邁瞬降到0	it went from 65 to zero .
我猛踩剎車	i slammed on the brakes .
我當時感覺到我的車的防抱死系統啟動了但車還在行駛並沒停下來的意思我也知道我的車停不了了安全氣囊也鼓了起來車報廢了但幸運的是沒有人受傷	i felt my car's defense launched , but the car is still there and it doesn't stop , and i knew that my car stopped and the airbags had summoned up , and that was wiped out , but fortunately no one was hurt .
但我根本不知道我前面那輛車要停而且我想我們可以比那做得更好	but i didn't know that i was going to stop in front of me , and i think we can do better than that .
我想我們透過實現 " 讓汽車之間對話 " 來改變我們的駕駛體驗	i think we can change our driving experience by releasing dialogue between cars .
我希望你們能思考片刻思考一下現在的駕駛體驗是怎麼樣的	i want you to think for a moment about what a driver experience looks like .
坐進車裡關上車門你就已經置身在一個玻璃氣泡中	you're sitting in a car , you close the door , you're already in a glass bubble .
你不能直接感受到你周圍的世界	you can't just feel the world around you .
因為你坐在車這樣一個不小的空間裡	because you're sitting in a very small space , like a car .

對吧 ? 你只能靠雙眼來導航	right ? you can navigate with your eyes .
對你別無他法眼睛並非是用來幹著活兒的但是有些事情你就必須得做 , 比方說 , 你想換個車道那你第一件要做的事是什麼	ignorantly , your eyes aren't meant to be alive , but some things you have to do , like , you want to swap lanes , so what's the first thing you have to do ?
將眼睛從車道上移開對	take your eyes off the lanes .

所有人都這麼做這是安全的駕駛方式	we're all doing this . it's a safe way of driving .
我們為什麼這麼做 ? 因為我們別無選擇我們必須作出一個抉擇是朝這兒看還是朝那兒看	why do we do this ? because we have no choice , and we have to make a decision about whether we look here or whether we look there .
我們通常都做得很好能夠很好的選擇我們要往哪個方向開	we're usually good at choosing where we're going to go .
但是偶然我們也會忘記一些事情	but incidentally , we'll forget a few things .

我們可以看到我們前面那輛車的速度看看前面那位什麼時候會啟動或停下	we can see the vehicle in front of us , and we can see when that person is activating or stopping in front of us .
假如那人的速度突然降到零 , 我就能知道了 。	if the speed of that person was breaking down to zero , i'd know .
利用運算代數以及預測模型我們能看見未來	using algorithms and prediction models , we can see the future .

你怎麼能預測未來呢太難了	how can you predict the future ? it's too hard .
事實上不難對於汽車來說這並非不可能	the fact is , it's not impossible for cars .
汽車是三維物體位置速度都是固定的	cars are threedimensional objects with a fixed speed .
行使在路上的時候	it's time for the road to go .
它們通常都是按照預先規劃好的道路行駛	they're usually traffic in preplaned roads .
未來想要預測汽車將要駛向什麼方向對之作出合理的預測並不困難	it's not hard to predict where cars are headed in the future .

在10 , 20 , 30英里前 , 有人看見過他 , 只要一輛車看見那個人將他的資訊置入地圖中 , 他的位置就會顯示在地圖上了位置 , 速度預測他將保持85英里的時速	in the last 10 , 20 , 30 miles , someone's seen him , just one car sees that person putting his information on the map , and he's going to show you where he is on the map , and it's going to predict his speed at 85 miles an hour .

貝基布蘭頓:我無家可歸的一年	becky brandon: i had been homeless for a year .
我是一個作家 , 一個新聞記者 , 我也是一位具有強烈求知慾的人 。 所以在做新聞記者的22年裡 , 我知道了很多新奇的事物 。	i'm a writer , i'm a journalist , i'm also a journalist , i'm an informed person , so over the 22 years as a journalist , i've known a lot of new things .
而三年前 , 我學會做的一件事就是變成隱形人 。	and three years ago , one of the things i learned to do was to become invisible .
我成了一個無家可歸的工作者 。	i became a homeless worker .
我辭掉了報紙編輯的工作在我父親那年二月去世之後我決定去旅行	i quit my newspaper editor's job , and after my father died in february of that year , i decided to travel .
他的去世對我打擊非常大 。	his death hit me so hard .
當時這麼做 , 是因為有很多我想去感知和處理的事 。	and this was because there were so many things i wanted to perceive and process .
旅遊時我天天都在露營 。 並且決定在休旅車裡住一年就當作是一段長期野營旅行 。	i've been camping every day while i've traveled , and decided to live for a year in a minivan for a longterm period of time .
所以 , 我就帶上我的貓 , 我的羅特威爾犬和露營的裝備裝載到1975產的雪佛萊旅遊車上 , 開車去看日落但當時完全沒想過三件嚴重的事	so i took my cat , my rottville and camp equipment to the 1975 schevley van and drove to the sunset at the time , but did not think of any three serious things .
一:社會將住房即使是很小的房間 , 和人的價值等同起來 。	number one: societies are just as valuable as even tiny rooms .
二:我沒有意識到其他人的負面言語對我們本身的影響是多麼嚴重 , 假如我們放任不管 。	two: i didn't realize how severe the negative speech on other people is on our own if we let it go .
三:我沒有意識到無家可歸是一種生活態度而不是一種生活方式 。	three: i'm not aware that homelessness is an attitude ; it's not a lifestyle .
一開始 , 住在車裡是很不錯的 。	at first , it's nice to live in a car .
我在露天洗澡 , 正常的去外面吃東西 。	i was showering all day , normally going outside and eating .
而且有時間去抒發情感 。	and then there's time to exchange emotions .
但是後來 , 因我父親去世而帶來的悲憤和痛沮開始加劇 。	but then , the anger and the pain that my father died began to frustrate .
我自由作家的工作結束了 。 我就需要去找一件全職工作來支付我的賬單 。	my free writer's job ends . i need to get a fulltime job to pay my bills .
從一個非常溫和的春天變到一個極其炎熱的夏天會怎樣呢 。	from a very mild summer , a very mild summer , to a very hot summer .
不管車停在哪都是難以忍受的不用說也很明顯我帶著一隻貓和一隻狗 , 而且非常的熱 。	it's kind of hard to bear around anywhere , and it's obvious that i'm carrying a cat and a dog , and it's very hot .
貓從車窗來回的跑 。	the cat runs back and forth from the window .
狗跑到了狗狗護理中心 。	the dog ran to the dog nurse's shop .
不管什麼時候 , 只要可以 , 我就會去用在辦公大樓和卡車車站裡員工用的淋浴 。	and whenever i did , i would use the showers at the office buildings and in truck stops for office staff .
或者在公共衛生間裡洗洗 。	or you can wash it in public health .
在夜裡車裡的溫度很少會降到華氏80度以下 , 這使我幾乎無法入睡 。	the temperature of the car in the night would rarely fall below 80 degrees fahrenheit , and it made me almost impossible to sleep .
食物在高溫下腐壞 。	food is rotting in the heat .
冷藏櫃裡的冰幾個小時就化完了 , 非常苦悶的時期 。	the ice in the refrigerated container passed away for hours , very painful time .
我沒錢找公寓 , 或者找不到讓我可以養狗和貓的地方 。	i couldn't find an apartment or i couldn't find a place where i could feed my dogs and cats .
我不想把它們拋棄 。 所以我繼續待在旅行車裡 。	i didn't want to give them up , so i stayed in a van .
但炎熱的天氣使我飽受折磨以至於在夜裡走50英尺到車外面的公共衛生間都懶的動 。 我用桶和垃圾袋當廁所 。	but thermal weather made me so sick at 50 feet out of the night , that the public health was lazy , and i was using buckets and garbage bags .
當冬天來臨的時候 , 溫度驟降到零度以下 。 然後就一直這麼冷 。	when winter came , the temperatures dropped below zero , and it stayed so cold .
我又遇到了一堆新問題 ,	i was running through a bunch of new questions .
每晚我的車都停在不同的地方 。 這樣才可以不讓警察發現以至於和警察爭吵 。	every night , my cars parked in different locations so that the police couldn't argue with the police .
當然 , 並不是每次都成功 。	of course , not always .
但是 , 我覺得我已無力掌控自己的生活了 。	but i feel like i've run out of control of my life .
我也不知道什麼時候或者是如何發生的 , 我這麼快就從一個有才的寫手 , 新聞從業者變成一個無家可歸 , 住在車裡的女人這簡直是快的難以置信 。	i don't know when or how it happened , soon i'd gone from being a talented writer to being homeless , from being a woman , who lived in a vehicle was incredibly fast .
我並沒有變 。 我的智商沒有降低 。	i wasn't changing . my iq was not lowering .
我的才能 , 我的正直 , 我的價值 , 所有關於我的這些東西都還是一樣 。	my talent , my integrity , my worth , everything about me remains the same .
但是從某種程度上 , 我還是改變了 ,	but in a way , i'm still changing .
我越來越沮喪 , 像一個漩渦一樣不斷地往下沉 。	i was getting frustrated , and like a spiral eddy , i kept going down .
後來有人介紹我去一個專為無家可歸之人開的健康診所 。	i was later introduced to a health clinic that i had been developing for a very specific homeless person .
我去了 。 我有三天都沒有洗澡了 ,	i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .
我和其他那些排隊的人一樣沮喪 , 身上的味道也很難聞 。	i'm as depressed as all those other queues , and smells are very difficult to smell .
我只是沒有喝醉或者興奮 。	i just wasn't drunk or excited .
當一些無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括一個以前在大學任教的教授 , 他們說: " 你不是無家可歸 , 你真正在這裡的原因是什麼 ? "	when the homeless people realized that , including a former professor back in college , said , " you're not homeless . what's the reason you're here ? "
其他的無家可歸的人不把我當作是無家可歸的人看待 。 但是我自己是這麼認為的 。	other homeless people don't see me as homeless people , but i do .

首先 , 他第一次使城市成長變成了可能不論地點、成為什麼規模和形狀的城市	first , he's the first person to make it possible to grow cities , regardless of what scale and shape they might be .

mit研究人員斯凱拉•蒂比茨從事自我裝配的研究一個取代建造東西的主意 , 我們能創建制作自己的材料 , 很像dna鏈打包的方式 。 目前還是一個巨大概念的早期階段 ; 蒂比茨向我們展示了三個還在實驗中的專案 , 我們可以一窺一個自我裝配的未來可能的樣子 。	mit researchers , skera tibitz , were involved with the idea of selfmodifying and building things , and we were able to create our own materials , much like the way dna chains are currently in the early stages of a big idea , and tibby is showing us three projects that are still under the experiment , so we could peer into what the future of selfrepairing could look like .
斯凱拉•蒂比茨:我們能製作可以製作自己的東西麼 ?	sk: can we make things that we can make ourselves ?
今天我想向各位展示未來我們製作東西的方式 。	today i'd like to show you how we make things in the future .
我相信很快我們的建築和機器將能自我組裝 , 自我複製和自我修復 。	i believe that soon our buildings and machines will selfassemble , selfreplicate and repair .
因此我要向各位展示我所認為的製造業的當前狀況 , 接著再將其與一些自然系統比較 。	so i'm going to show you what i think of as a current state of manufacturing and then compare it to some natural systems .
那麼在當前的製造業中 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間 , 50萬至上百萬個部分 , 非常複雜 , 使用了在鋼鐵 , 混凝土和玻璃方面的新技術 。	so in the current manufacturing industry , we had skyscrapers two and a half years , 500 to a half million parts , very complicated , using new technologies in steel , concrete and glass .
我們有令人激動的機器 , 可以帶我們進入太空五年時間 , 兩百五十萬個部分 。	we have an exciting machine that can take us into space for five years , 2 . 5 million parts .
但另一方面 , 如果看看自然系統 , 我們有擁有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 能在一萬納秒內摺疊起來 , 我們能在大約一小時內對帶有三十億鹼基對的dna進行復制 。	but on the other hand , if you look at the natural system , we have two million types of proteins that fold up in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , and we can renaisse with three billion base pairs of dna in about an hour .
這就是我們自然系統的複雜性 , 但它們非常高效 , 比我們建造的任何東西都要高效 , 比我們能建造的任何東西都要複雜 。	it's the complexity of our natural system , but they're very efficient , more efficient than anything we build , more sophisticated than anything we can build .
它們在能源方面更加高效 。	they're more efficient in terms of energy .
它們很少犯錯 。	they make very few mistakes .
他們能自我修復保持長壽 。	they can repair their longevity .
關於自然系統有件超級有意思的事情 。	now , there's something really interesting about natural systems .
如果我們能將其轉換為我們的建築環境 , 那麼我們構建事物的方式就會有很大的潛力 。	and if we can convert that into our built environment , then there's tremendous potential in how we construct things .
我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。	i think the key to that is selfassembly .
如果我們想要在自身的身體環境中利用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。	if we want to use our selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there are four key factors .
第一個是 , 我們需要解碼我們所要建造的東西的所有的複雜度也就是我們的建築和機器 。	the first one is that we need to decode all the complexity of what we're building , our buildings and machines .
我們需要把它們解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們的建築運作的dna 。	we need to code them into simple sequences that are essentially the dna of how our buildings work .
接著我們需要可程式設計的部分這部分能接受這一序列並用於摺疊或是重塑 。	and then we need the programmable parts that can accept the sequence and fold it and reshap it .
我們需要一些能量來進行啟用 , 使我們的這些部分能夠依照程式摺疊起來 。	we need some energy to run , so that these parts of us can code and fold them .
我們需要一些型別的糾錯冗餘以保證我們成功建造的就是我們想要的 。	we need some redundancy to guarantee that what we're successful at is what we want .
因此 , 我要向各位展示一些我和我的同事正在進行的要實現這種自我組裝的未來的專案 。	so i'm going to show you some projects that my colleagues and i are working on to realize this selfassembly future .
頭兩個專案是macrobot和decibot 。	the first two projects were macrobot and decibot .
這些專案都是大規模可重構機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。	all of these projects are reconstructing robots at eight feet , 12 feet long proteins .
它們嵌入機電裝置 , 感測器 。	they're embedded in mechanical appliances , sensors .
你需要把想要摺疊的方式解碼成 , 解碼成一系列角度負120度 , 負120度 , 0度 , 0度 , 120度 , 負120度 , 這類的東西 ; 一系列角度 , 或轉向 , 可以用電線把這個次序傳過去 。	you have to decode the way you want to fold it into a series of angles that are 120 degrees , negative 120 degrees , zero , minus 120 degrees , negative , 120 degrees , minus 120 degrees , that sort of thing ; a series of angles , or rotations , where you can get that wire passing through the sequence .
每個單元獲取自己的訊息比如負120.它進行旋轉 , 檢查是否旋轉到位然後把序列傳給它的鄰居 。	each unit gets its own message , like minus 120 . it rotates , checks if it spins to its neighbor and passes the sequence to its neighbor .
有許多傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師為這個專案工作 。	there are some brilliant scientists , engineers , designers working on this project .
我認為這一專案真的揭示出:這真的可擴充套件麼 ?	and i think the project really reveals this: is this really a scalable thing to do ?
我是說 , 花費數千美元許多人時來製造這個八英尺的機器人 。	i mean , it costs thousands of dollars and lots of people to build this eightfoot robot .
我們真的能擴大它麼 ? 我們真的能在每個部分中都嵌入機器人麼 ?	can we actually expand it ? can we actually embedded a robot in every part ?
下一個問題是看看被動性 , 或被動地嘗試讓重組具有可程式設計性 。	the next question was looking at passive or passive attempts to recombine reforms with programmable design .
但它更進了一步 , 它嘗試進行實際計算 。	but it went further , and it tried to do actual computation .
基本上嵌入了多數計算的基礎構建模組 , 數字邏輯閘 , 直接進入各個部分 。	it's essentially embedded in most computational building modules , the digital logic gate , directly into all parts .
這是與非門 。	it's a nationstate .
每個要用於計算的門上都有一個四面體 , 有兩個輸入四面體 。	there's a tetrahedron on each door to the calculation that has two inputs .
其中一個是來自使用者的輸入 , 就像你在構建磚塊 。	one of them is the input from the user , just like you're building bricks .
另一個是來之前前放好的一塊磚的輸入 。	the other is the input of a brick that came in before .
接著它會給出三維空間的輸出 。	and then it will give the threedimensional output .
這意味著使用者以他們想要的方式堆砌磚塊 。	it means that users build bricks in the way they want .
它依據之前所做的和你的指令進行計算 。	it's calculated based on what you've done and what your instructions have been doing .
現在它開始在三維空間內移動上或者下 。	and now it starts moving up or down in three dimensions .
看左面 , [1 , 1]的輸入等於0輸出 , 表示向下 。	look to the left . [1 , 1 . ] input is 0 output , and that's down .
在右邊 , [0 , 0]的輸入是1輸出 , 表示向上 。	on the right , [0 , zero] input is an output , upwards .
因此這真正的的意味是我們的結構中現在包含了我們想要構建的藍圖 。	so that really means that our structure now contains blueprints that we want to build .
因此關於想要構建的事物的資訊已經全部嵌入其中 。	so the information about what's going to be built has embedded in it .
這意味著我們有了某種形式的自我複製 。	what that means is that we have some form of selfreplication .
對這種情況 , 我稱之為自我導向複製 , 因為你的結構中包含了精確的藍圖 。	in this case , i call it selfdirected replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .
如果遇到錯誤 , 你可以替換一個部分 。	if you're having an error , you can replace parts .
所有的本地資訊都嵌入其中 , 告訴你如何修復它 。	all the local information is embedded in it and telling you how to repair it .
因此你有個可以攀爬的東西 , 能讀出它並一個一個的輸出 。	so you have something that climbs , you can read it and have an output .
它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外部指令輸入 。	it's embedded directly ; there's no external command input .
我要展示的最後一個專案名為偏心鏈條 , 它可能是我們現在看到的被動自我裝配系統中最令人激動的例子 。	the final project i'm going to show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example of what we're seeing here in this automatic rationing system .
它具有可重構性和可程式設計性使它成了為了一個完全地被動系統 。	it has reconstructability and programmability that makes it a passive system for fully occurring .
基本上就是你有了一連串的元素 。	it's basically a series of elements that you have .
每個元素都是完全相同的 , 且它們是偏心的 。	each element is identical , and they're biased .
每個鏈條 , 或每個元素想要向右轉或是向左轉 。	each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .
如果你要裝配鏈條 , 需要為它程式設計 。	if you want the chain , you need to program it .
要告訴每個單元是要左轉還是右轉 。	to tell each unit to go left or right .
當你搖動這個鏈條時 , 它就摺疊起來程式設計你所為它編碼的任何結構因此這種情況下 , 一個螺旋體 , 火這種情況 , 兩個相連的立方體 。	when you shake the chain , it folds it up into whatever structure you encode , so in this case , a spiral , fire , two cubes that are connected .
基本上你可以在三維空間內程式設計或是一維、二維這鏈條是完全被動的 。	you can essentially program or onedimensional design within a threedimensional space , and the chain of twodimensional is completely passive .
這向我們預示了怎樣的未來呢 ?	what is the future that's predicted to us ?
我認為這告訴我們這些在我們的身體結構、我們的建築和機器中這種自我裝配、自我複製和自我修復的可能性 。	i think it's telling us the possibilities of selforganizing , selfreplication and selfrepairing in our bodies , our architecture and our machines .
在這些部分中有新的可程式設計性 。	there's new programmability in these parts .
從中你能獲得計算的新可能性 。	you've got new possibilities for computing .
我們將有空間計算 。	we're going to have spatial computing .
想象一下我們的建築、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚塊都能進行實際計算 。	imagine our buildings , our bridges , our machines all bricks are actually calculating .
多麼令人驚奇的平行計算和分散式計算能力和新的設計可能性啊 。	it's an amazing parallel calculation and distributed computing and new design possibilities .
這是項令人激動的潛力 。	it's an exciting potential .
我認為這些我向各位展示的專案僅僅是邁向未來的一小步 , 如果我們為一個新的自我組裝的世界實現了這些新技術的話 。	and i think these projects that i'm showing you are just a tiny step towards the future , if we've implemented these new technologies for a new selfassembly world .
我們已踏上過月球 , 我們已測繪了大陸 , 我們甚至已去過海底最深處--兩次 。 還剩下什麼值得我們的下一代去探索 ? 生物學家和內森•沃爾夫提出了這樣的答案:幾乎所有事物 。 " 我們可以從那小到看不見的世界開始 " , 他說 。	we've moved onto the moon , we've mapped the continent , we've even been to the bottom of the sea twice . what's left for our children ? biologists and nathan wolff have given the answer to the question , " almost anything . "
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	so , you know , lotity and lots and lots and lots of stuff .
內森•沃爾夫:還有什麼值得探索 ?	nathan wolf: what else is it worth exploring ?
最近我去了威斯康星州的伯洛伊特市 。	recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .
我去那裡是為了紀念一名20世紀的探險家 , 羅伊•查普曼•安德魯斯 。	i went there to honor a 20thcentury explorer , roy chapman andrews .
當他在美國自然歷史博物館的時候 , 安德魯斯領導了一系列對未知領域的探險 , 比如說在這裡的戈壁灘 。	when he was in the american museum of natural history , andrews led a series of expeditions to the unknown , like here in the gobim beach .
他是個了不起的人物 。	he's a wonderful human being .
他後來據說是印第安娜瓊斯角色的原型 。	it was later said to be the prototype of the indiana jones character .
當我在威斯康星州的伯洛伊特市的時候 , 我給一群中學學生上了一堂公開課 。	when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i opened up a group of middle school students .
我現在想告訴你們 , 如果真的有什麼比在ted做演講還難的話 , 那就是嘗試保持他們的注意力一群上千個12歲的孩子 , 並保持45分鐘 。	and i want to tell you now that if there's anything more difficult than giving a talk at ted , it's to try and keep their attention for a bunch of 12yearolds for 45 minutes .
在我講完之後 , 他們問了很多問題 , 但有一個讓我自始至終難以忘記 。	after i finished my lecture , they asked a lot of questions , but there was one i'd never forget .
有個小女孩站起來 , 問了一個問題: " 我們該去哪裡探索呢 ? "	and this little girl stood up and she asked the question , " where should we go to explore this ? "
我想我們中的絕大多數有種觀念 , 那就是 , 地球上的大探索時代已經結束 , 我們的下一代人應該去外太空或者海洋最深處從而去尋找值得探索的東西 。	i think most of us have the concept that the age of exploration on earth is over , that our next generation should go to outer space or the deepest part of the ocean and be able to find something worth exploring .
但真的是這樣嗎 ?	but is that true ?
真的沒有重要的地方留給我們探索了嗎 ? 整個地球上都沒有 ?	does it really matter that we explore that we haven't gotten anywhere on earth ?
這讓我回憶起我最喜歡的生物領域的探險家之一 。	this reminds me of one of my favorite biological explorers .
他是位未知世界的探索家 , 馬丁努斯•威廉•拜耶林克 。	he's an explorer of the unknown world , martin nus william beyelyk .
拜葉林克當初想找出引起菸草花葉病的原因 。	bayalink , who started out looking for the causes of tobaccofree leaflies .
他提取了受過感染的菸草汁液 , 然後讓這些汁液經過一層比一層更細的過濾 。	he extracted the infected tobacco sap , and then he released it through a layer of detail that was more filtered than a layer .
他得出一個結論 , 剩下的裡面一定有什麼東西它們比那時最小的已知的生命形態--細菌 , 還要小 。	he came to the conclusion that there must be something left in there that was smaller than all the life that was then the smallest known bacteria , smaller .
他給這個神秘的東西起了個名字	he has a name for this mysterious thing .
叫它們 , 病毒在拉丁文裡是 " 毒藥 " 的意思 。	tell them it means " poison " in latin .
在發現病毒之後 , 拜耶林克為我們打開了一個全新的世界 。	after discovering the virus , bayeque opened us a whole new world .
我們現在知道病毒構成我們星球上絕大部分的遺傳資訊超過所有其他生命的遺傳資訊的總和 。	we now know that viruses make up most of our genetic information on our planet than the sum of all other life's genetic information .
而且顯然已經出現了無數有關病毒的切實應用在這個世界上--像天花的根除 , 子宮癌的疫苗的降臨--我們現在知道它大部分是由乳頭瘤病毒引起的 。	and apparently , there have been so many cases of virus applications in the world things like the roots of smallpox eradication , the demise of cervical cancer we know now mostly caused by mammogram viruses .
而且拜耶林克的發現可不是500年前的事情 。	and that's not 500 years ago by baylink's discovery .
拜耶林克發現病毒這件事也就發生於100多年前 。	this also happened more than 100 years ago by bayerine found out about it .
也就是說當汽車都已經出現在世的時候 , 我們還不知道這種構成了我們星球上大部分的遺傳資訊的生物 。	and what that means is that when cars are dead , we don't yet realize that this makes up most of the genetic information we have on our planet .
我們現在有些很了不起的工具來幫助我們探索未知世界 , 像基因深度測序 , 可以讓我們不只是停留在表面來看自某個特定物種的獨立基因組 , 而是研究整個基因組--我們身體裡面和周邊無處不在的微生物群落 , 並且記錄下這些物種的遺傳資訊 。	we now have some incredible tools to help us explore the unknown world , like the deep sequencing of genes that allow us to not just pause on the surface to see individual genomes from a particular species , but to study entire genomes of our bodies and our surrounding microbial communities and record the genetic information of these species .
我們可以應用這些技術來研究從土壤到皮膚和它們中間的一切 。	we can use these technologies to study everything from soil to skin and everything in between .
在我所在的機構裡面 , 我們現在經常這麼做 , 來尋找暴發的原因 , 那些我們還不清楚的原因.	in my institutions , which we do now , we often do this to search for causes of abuse , which we don't know .
稍微給你們講下這是怎麼做的 , 想象下從你們每個人那裡取一個鼻腔分泌物標本	and just to give you a sense of how this is done , this is to imagine where each one of you is taking a nasal secretion label .
像這種事是我們經常做的 , 為了尋找呼吸道病毒 , 像流行性感冒病毒 。	and things like this are the kinds of things we do all the time in search of respiratory viruses like flu .
我們首先看到的是海量的遺傳資訊 。	the first thing we saw was the volume of genetic information .
如果我們開始仔細看看這些遺傳資訊 , 我們會看到一些常見的資訊當然了 , 有很多人類的遺傳資訊 , 但也有很多細菌和病毒的資訊 , 大部分是你鼻子裡面完全無害的東西 。	if we start looking at these genetic information , we're going to see some common information , and of course , a lot of human genetic information , but there's a lot of information about bacteria and viruses , mostly harmless things in your nose .
但我們也會看到一些非常非常讓人吃驚的東西 。	but we also see something very , very surprising .
當我們開始研究這些資訊 , 我們會發現你鼻子裡面20%的遺傳資訊跟我們所見過的東西--任何植物 , 動物 , 真菌或者細菌 , 都對不上號 。	and when we started looking at this information , we would see that 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose is introduced to everything we've seen in plants , animals , fungi or bacteria .
我們基本上對這些一無所知 。	we know essentially nothing about it .
我們這裡的一小部分研究這些資料的人們 , 稱呼這些資訊為生物暗物質 。	a small portion of the people that we're here studying this data , we call biological dark matter .
我們知道以前從未見過這些生物暗物質 ; 這似乎可以被稱之為我們自己遺傳資訊裡的未知大陸 。	we knew we'd never met these biological dark matters ; it seemed to be called the unknown continent of our own genetic information .
而且數量非常之多 。	and there's a lot of them .
如果你認為你鼻子裡面20%的遺傳資訊有很多生物暗物質 , 那當我們看你內臟的時候 , 那有將近40%到50%的生物暗物質 。	if you think 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose has plenty of biological dark matter , then when we look at the heart , there's almost 40 to 50 percent biological dark matter .
即使在相對無菌的血液裡 , 也有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質--無法被歸類 , 無法被判別類別 , 跟我們所見過的東西都不同 。	even in the relatively sterile blood , dark matter is dark matter can't be classified , can't be categorized , can't be categorized for anything that we've seen before .
開始我們以為這是人為的東西 。	we started with this idea of human beings .
這些基因深度測序工具相當比較新 。	these gene deep sequencing tools are relatively new .
但當它們變得越來越來精確 , 我們認為這些資訊是一種新的生命 , 或者至少某一部分是種生命 。	but as they get more and more precise , we think that information is a new form of life , or at least a part of it , is a form of life .
即使這些關於解釋生物暗物質的存在的假設還處於嬰兒期 , 一個讓人非常非常激動的可能性存在著:那就是藏在這個生命裡面 , 在這些遺傳資訊裡 , 有一種沒有被識別的生命的標識 。	and even though these assumptions about the presence of biological dark matter are in infancy , an incredibly exciting possibility exists which lies in this life , in these genetic informations , a mark of life without identification .

stephenhawking觀點中其中一個正確面--我的意思是 , 這是正確的 , 但是著重點是錯的 。 其中一個正確面是它並沒有倚賴任何特殊的物理學 。 沒有特殊的放寬 , 沒有奇蹟發生 。 它的發生只依賴於我們現在富有的三種東西 。	one of the right things about the stephen hawking perspective i mean , this is true , but the point is that it's wrong . one of the correct things is that it doesn't rely on any special physics . there's no special width , no miracles . it just happens to be based on three things that we're rich now .
