換句話說 , 這是一個關於知識的問題 , 而不是關於資源 。	in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .
同樣 , 如果我們可以做到的話 , 那麼我們將自動獲得能源供給 , 因為這裡的變化將是核反應堆--證據 ?	similarly , if we can do that , we'll automatically have an energy supply , because what's going to happen here is a nuclear reactor evidence ?
還是一樣 , 對人類的感官來說那裡漆黑一片 。 但是你所需要做的是拿起一個望遠鏡 , 甚至是今天的技術設計 , 往外看去 , 你會看到我們從這兒看到的同樣的星系 。	again , it's dark out there for human senses , but what you need to do is to pick up a telescope , even a modern technology , and look out , and you'll see the same galaxies that we see from here .
如果你有一個更強大的望遠鏡 , 你將能看到恆星和行星 。	if you have a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars and planets .
在那些星系裡 , 你可以進行天體物理學研究 , 瞭解物理定律 。	in those galaxies , you can do astrophysics study and understand the laws of physics .
在你所處的位置 , 你可以製造粒子加速器 , 研究初級粒子物理學 , 化學等 。	in your position , you can make particle accelerators , study primary particle physics , chemistry , etc .
也許最難做的科學研究是生物學實地考察 , 因為需要花費數百萬年才能往返最近的有生命的星球 。	perhaps the most difficult scientific studies are biology field trips , because it takes millions of years to get to a nearest living planet .
但是我必須告訴你--對不起 , richard--但是我從來都不是那麼喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以每數百萬年才進行一次 。	but i have to tell you sorry richard but i don't really like biology field trips so much , and i think we can do it every millions of years .
因此事實上 , 星系間空間並不具備創造開放式知識的前提條件 。 任何一個這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙中任何地方 , 都可以成為跟我們一樣的中心 , 如果履行這一計劃的知識確實存在的話 。	so , in fact , intergalactic space does not have the prerequisites to create open knowledge , and any cube , anywhere in the universe , can be a center just like us , if the knowledge of the project really exists .
因此我們並不是唯一熱情好客的地方 。	so we're not the only place where we're passionate about it .
如果星系間空間可以創造出一串開放式的解說 , 那麼幾乎其它所有的環境都是可以的 。 地球也一樣 。 被汙染的地球也是一樣 。	if intergalactic space creates an opensource list , then virtually every other setting can , the same way the earth can , too: contaminated earth .
而限制性因素 , 這裡和那裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充沛 , 而是知識 , 非常匱乏 。	and the limiting factors , here and there , are not resources because they're so abundant , but knowledge , they're scarce .
這樣一個知識型的宇宙觀也許--我認為應該--讓我們感覺非常不平凡 。 但同時也讓我們感覺到自己的脆弱 , 因為這也意味著如果沒有那些必需的具體的知識來幫助我們應對宇宙中源源不斷地挑戰 , 我們將無法生存 。	this cosmic view of knowledge may seem to me it should make us feel very extraordinary , but it also makes us feel vulnerable , because it means that if we don't have all the specific knowledge we need to respond to constant challenges of the universe , we will not survive .
僅僅是幾光年外的一個超新星爆炸 , 我們都將必死無疑 。	it's just a supernova explosion a few lightyears away , and we're all going to be dead .
martinrees最近剛寫了一本關於我們人類對於所有事物的脆弱性的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗事故 , 還有最重要的擁有大規模殺傷性武器的恐怖主義 。	martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all things , from astrophysics to scientific experimental occurrences , and most importantly , terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .
他認為人類文明只有50%的機率可以存活過這個世紀 。	he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .
我想他晚些時候會在這個會上給大家講述 。	i think he's going to tell you later about this conference .
但是我認為這一問題並不適合用機率來描述 。	but i don't think that's the right question to describe probabilities .
但是我同意他就此的看法 。 我們可以生存下去 , 我們也可能不會存續 。	but i agree with him , and we can survive , and we may not survive .
但是這並不取決於機率 , 而是我們是否可以及時創造出相關的知識 。	but it doesn't depend on probability , but on whether we can create relevant knowledge in time .
這種危險肯定不是前所未有的 。 物種一直都在滅絕 。	this danger is not certainly unprecedented . species have been extinct .
文明也會終止 。 絕大多數存在過的物種和文明都以成歷史 。	civilizations are ending . the vast majority of species and civilizations exist in history .
如果我們想成為例外的話 , 邏輯上來看我們唯一的希望是利用將我們這個種群和文明與其他物種區別開的這個特徵 , 與其他一切都區別開的這個特徵 。 也就是 , 我們與物理定律得特殊關係 。 我們創造新的解釋和知識的能力--成為存在的中心 。	if we want to be the exception , then logically , our only hope is to distinguish the features that distinguish our species and civilization from all other species , which is that we have a special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations and knowledge to be the hub of existence .
讓我將此運用到當前的一個論戰中 , 不是因為我想提議任何特定的解決方法 , 而只是用來闡明我所要講述的一些事 。	let me apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to propose any particular solution , but just to illustrate what i'm going to talk about .
這個論戰就是全球暖化 。	this controversy is global warming .
我是一個物理學家 , 但我並不是此領域的物理學家 。 就全球暖化來說 , 我只是個門外漢 。 對一個門外漢來說理智的做法是嚴肅對待權威的科學理論 。 而根據這一理論 , 已經太晚了 , 災難在所難免 。	i'm a physicist , but i'm not the physicist in this field , and as a global warming , i'm just an outsider , and the idea that reason has to do with a serious scientific theory of authority , and it's already too late , and disaster strikes .
因為 , 如果我們目前最好的選擇是阻止二氧化碳排放的話 , 例如透過東京議定書之類的 , 限制經濟活動 , 以及花費千億美元等巨大的代價 , 那麼不管如何衡量 , 這就已經是一個災難了 。	because if our current best options are to stop carbon dioxide emissions from things like tokyo protocol , restricting economic activity and costing hundreds of billions of dollars , then it is a disaster , no matter what .
倡議的行動甚至都不是為解決問題 , 而只是稍微推遲災難的到來 。 因此災難在所難免 , 一切都已晚 , 或在所有人意識到這個危險之前就已經太晚了 。	it's not even an act of catastrophe , it's just slightly too late to disaster , it's already too late , or it's too late to be aware of the dangers .
上世紀70年代的時候也許就已經太晚了 , 那時候最先進的科學理論告訴我們工業排放將促成一個新的冰河世紀 , 數十億的人類將從此滅亡 。	it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the most advanced scientific theory told us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age , billions of people would die .
這一教訓對我來說清晰可見 , 我不明白為什麼它沒有傳達至公眾辯論 。	the lesson was clear to me , and i don't know why it didn't communicate public debate .
事實是我們不可能永遠知道 。 當我們知道有一個災難將要降臨 , 應對這個災難的成本要比災難本身小 , 那麼就真的沒有什麼好爭論的 。	the fact is that we can't always know , and when we know that there's a disaster that's going to come down and respond to this catastrophe , there's actually no good argument about what it takes to deal with it .
但是沒有任何預防措施 , 或者預防原則可以幫助我們避免我們還沒有預測到的問題 。	but no precautions , no precautionary principle can help us avoid problems we haven't anticipated yet .
因此我們需要準備好去解決問題 , 而不僅僅是避免問題 。	so we need to be ready to solve problems , not just avoid problems .
一盎司的預防等於一盎司的解決 , 這是事實 , 但是這只是在我們知道預防什麼的情況下 。	an ounce of prevention equals an ounce of solving , which is true , but it's only when we know what to prevent .
如果你的鼻子被打了一拳 , 醫學不會教你如何閃躲拳頭 。	if you're punched with your nose , medicine does not teach you how to get out of your punches .
如果醫學不再研究治病的方法 , 而是僅僅研究預防 , 那麼它將幾乎一事無成 。	if medicine stops studying treatment and instead studying prevention , it's almost nothing .
目前整個世界都在不計成本地忙著計劃來促成氣體排放量的減少 。	now the entire world is working on planning to drive decrease in gas emissions at scale .
而它應該趕緊計劃如何降低溫度 , 以及計劃如何在溫度升高之後如何生存 。 不是不計成本 , 而是有效地、廉價的計劃 。 而這樣的一些計劃已經存在了 , 比如在太空中放置大批鏡子來將太陽光反射出去 , 以及刺激海洋生物消費更多的二氧化碳 。	and it should be rushing up to the temperature plans to reduce the survival of the temperature rising , not in terms of cost , but inexpensively and cheaply planned , and some of those programs already exist , such as placing clouds of mirrors in space to reflect sunlight and stimulate more carbon dioxide .
而目前 , 這些都只是邊緣研究 。	and so far , this is all fringe research .
人類在應對這個問題或者廣義上來說這些問題的時候 , 它們起不到核心作用 。	when human beings address this problem or , broadly speaking , they don't have the core effects .
對於我們並未知覺的問題 , 糾錯的能力--不是無限期的躲過期發生的絕對好運--是我們唯一的希望 , 不僅僅是為解決問題 , 而是為生存 。	the ability to get things wrong about what we don't even know about , isn't the endless hiding it's our only hope , not just for problems , but for survival .
我們應該拿起兩塊石碑 , 在上邊刻上銘文 。	we should pick up two of them , carve inscriptions up above us .

另外一塊刻上 " 問題是不可避免的 " 。	on the other panel , carve: " the problem is inevitable . "

我想說 , 我們可以把抽象化為實際或者說 , 如果我們給予人民更多選擇給予領導者更多選擇 , 領導者在很多國家也是人民麼	i mean , we can turn abstract into practical , or , if we give people more choices , more choices to leaders , and more choices , and more leaders , in many countries , are people .

這些的成功引起共識帶領整個經濟體制走向市場經濟	these successes have led consensus to consensus leading the entire economy to the market economy .
現在中國的這些例子證明以下幾點:	now , these examples in china are proof of the following point .
一:留給人民自由	one: be free to the people .
二:在恰當的規模下操作	two: operate at the right scale .
如果你想在一個村莊改變體制 , 可以 , 但一個村的規模太小了不能帶給你如同讓百萬人一樣的效應在優質體制的治理下	if you want to change the institutions in a village , yes , but the scale of a village is too small to bring you the effects of a million people under highquality institutions .
另一方面 , 一下子改變全國的體制又太大了	on the other hand , the system is too large to change the country .

但像城市就能給你這些機會來建立新領域開拓新體制 , 人們可以選擇	but just like cities can give you these opportunities to create new domains , new institutions that people can choose .
並且足夠大大到我們能得到應有的當百萬人在新體制治理下應有的效應	and it's big enough to get the sustained effects that the millions should have in a new institutional rule .

工作很艱難 , 我們乘著一艘帆船某種程度上我們想透過它激起年輕人投身科學的興趣	it's very tough . we're shipping , in a way , in a way , in a way that we're interested in , in the science of young people .
實驗其實非常簡單	the experiment was very simple .
採集海水 , 過濾用不同的過濾器採集不同大小的生物然後把它們的dna帶回羅克韋爾的實驗室在那裡我們可以每24小時測完一億字元的遺傳編碼	you take seawater , you filter it , you take different creatures , you take their dna , you take it back to the lab of roxville , where we can detect 100 million letters of genetic code every 24 hours .
透過這些我們已經有了一些驚人的發現	and we've made some remarkable discoveries through this .
比如我們眼睛裡的視色素之前認為自然界中只有一到兩種生物擁有和我們一樣的視色素	for instance , our eyes pigment used to think that there's only one or two species in nature that have exactly the same optics as ours .
但後來發現在溫暖海區的上層海水中幾乎每個物種都擁有這類光受體並利用陽光作為能量來源和交流工具	but it turns out that in the warm waters , almost every species has this type of light receptors and uses sunlight as an energy source and communication tool .
僅僅一個採集點 , 從一桶水中我們就能發現1300萬個新基因相當於5萬個新種	a single mining point , from a bucket of water , we discovered that 13 million new genes equivalent to 50 , 000 new species .
藉助來自斯隆基金會的資助我們已經將研究擴充套件到空氣中	with funding from the sloan foundation , we've expanded research into air .
我們正在測算 , 在我們每天呼吸的空氣中漂浮著多少病毒和細菌特別是在飛機和禮堂等封閉環境中	we're working on calculating how many viruses and bacteria are floating in the air we breathe , especially closed environments in airplanes and auditoriums .
我們透過一些簡單的儀器進行過濾在紐約市某棟建築的頂上僅用一天我們就過濾出數十億計的微生物	we filtered billions of microbes on top of a building in new york city just one day , and we filtered out billions of microbes .
目前我們正在對它們進行測序	we're actually sequencing them now .
單純從資料蒐集方面僅僅在加拉帕戈斯群島我們就發現幾乎每200英里我們都能從採集的樣品中看到巨大的多樣性	simply collecting data , just in the galapagos islands , we found that almost every 200 miles we could see enormous diversity in a sample of data .
不同的溫度梯度或許可以部分解釋這種多樣性	the different temperature gradients may well be able to explain this diversity .
這是一張基於溫度的衛星圖片紅色表示溫暖區域藍色表示冷的區域我們發現 , 在溫暖海水中獲得樣品與冷海水中的樣品在物種的豐富程度上具有極大的差異	this is a satellite image based on the temperatures and the red shows warm regions and the cool regions , and what we're finding is that there's a huge difference between samples and samples in warm waters in the abundance of species .
另一個讓我們感到驚奇的事情是這些光受體能探測到不同波長的光而我們能透過它們的氨基酸序列來推測這一過程	the other thing that's surprising to us is that these light receptors can detect light from wavelengths , and we can extrapolate that through their amino acid sequ
不同區域之間 , 它們也差別巨大	they're also enormously different in different areas .
或許不是很讓人驚奇在幾乎是幽藍的深海里光受體傾向於 " 看 " 到藍光	it's not surprising that light receptors in most ufos receptors tend to see blue light .
而當週圍存在大量葉綠素的時候它們則 " 看 " 到許多綠光	and when there's lots of chlorophyll around them , they're going to look at lots of green light .
在向較極端的紅外和紫外波段移動時光受體的差別可能更大	at the extremes of infrared and ultraviolet waves , the light receptors may be much larger .
為了對我們採集的所有基因進行評估我們彙總了所有資料包括到目前為止考察所得的所有資料代表了地球上超過一半的基因資料總共約2900萬個基因	in order to conduct all of the genes that we've collected , we've combined all the data , including all of the data we've collected so far , that represents more than 29 million genetic data on the planet .
我們把這些基因放入基因家族中試圖回答:我們是發現了已知基因家族中的新成員還是發現了新的基因家族 ?	we took those and put them into the genomic family to try and answer: did we find new members of the known cognitive family , or did we find new families ?
結果表明我們找到了大約5萬個主要的基因家族但我們從環境中獲得的每個新樣品都只是對這些新基因家族的線性補充	it turns out we've got about 50 , 000 major families in genomic families , but every new sample we have in the environment is just a linear supply of these new genomic families .
因此我們正處在發現地球生命及其組成部分和基因基礎的最初階段	so we're in the earliest phase of discovering life on earth and its component parts of genetics .
我們來看下所謂的進化樹我們人類就在右上角 , 和動物們在一起	if we look at the evolutionary trees , we humans are up in the upper righthand corner with animals .
在動物界約2900萬個基因中我們的基因組才僅僅擁有24000個基因	it only has 24 , 000 genes in the animal kingdom .
如果把所有的動物算在一起我們與之分享著不到30000可能在1.2萬或再多數千的不同的基因家族	if we count all the animals together , we share less than 3 , 000 families with each other , at 1 . 2 , 000 , or more , thousands of different gene families .
現在我不僅僅將這些基因視為進化的設計元件	now i'm not just looking at these genes as evolutionary design components .
而且我們要從 " 基因中心觀點 " 或許要追溯到理查德•道金斯的理論而非 " 基因組中心觀點 " 來思考它們對這些基因元件的構造方式是不同的	and we're going to go from a genecentric viewpoint , back to richard dawkins' theory rather than a genomecentric view , to thinking about the ways in which these components are constructed .
合成dna , 即人工合成dna的能力在過去的十年或二十年裡與dna測序的能力在某種程度上是同步發展的而且都變得越來越快速和廉價	synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has been in the past decade or two , and the ability to sequence dna sequencing has been in some ways synchronized rapidly and cheaper .
有關合成基因組的想法是在1995年我們對第二個基因組即生殖道支原體測序的時候想到的	the idea about synthetic genomes was that in 1995 , when we were thinking about the second genitalia , the genitalia p . c . , were sequenced .
我們還製作了相當不錯的t恤寫著 , " 我愛惜我的生殖器 "	we also made a pretty nice tshirt , which says , " i love my genitalia . "
這其實只不過是個微小的生物	it's just a tiny creature .
卻擁有近500個基因	they have almost 500 genes .
嗜血桿菌擁有1800個基因	haemophilus has 1 , 800 genes .
我們提出疑問如果某物種需要800個基因 , 另一種需要500個是否能用一套更小的基因組成一個微小的可運作生命系統	we wondered if one species needs 800 genes , another species needs 500 , if one , to use a smaller set of genomes to build a smaller operating system .
於是我們開始做轉座子的突變發生	so we started making the mutations of the seat .
轉座子是隨機插入遺傳編碼之中的短的dna片段	the concoction is a short piece of dna that randomly inserts a genetic code .
如果轉座子插入到基因中間 , 就會擾亂基因的功能	if you plug in the middle of the genome , it disrupts the function of the gene .
因此我們找出所有能夠接受轉座子插入的基因併為這些 " 非必需基因 " 製作了 " 地圖 "	so we figured out all of the genes that could get transplants inserted into one of these " nonnecessary genes " maps .
但結果我們發現環境對此的影響非常關鍵我們只能根據環境中確實存在的條件來定義必需和非必需基因	but as it turns out , the environmental impact is critical , and we can only define the necessity and the necessity of the conditions in the environment .
我們還試圖做一個更直觀的研究對13個有親緣關係的生物我們試圖比較它們的基因組 , 看它們是否有相同之處	we also tried to do a more intuitive study of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare their genomes to see if they had the same thing .
於是我們得到了這些重疊的圓圈 , 我們發現只有173個基因在這所有13種生物中是相同的	so we got these overlapping circles , and we found that only 173 genes were identical in all 13 species .
如果忽略掉一個細胞內寄生物的話這個基因庫還能擴充套件一點當我們審視核心的一組約310個基因時基因庫擴大更多	if we ignore the intraception of a single parasite in cells , this gene pool can also expand a bit , and when we look at a core set of about 310 genes , the gene pool expands even more .
因此我們認為可以從最少500個基因擴充套件或縮小取決你怎麼看這個問題到約300到400個基因	so we thought that we could expand the package from the minimum amount of 500 genes , or shrink it , to something like 300 to 400 genes .
證明這些理論的唯一方法是以這些基因人工構建一個染色體而且我們必須用基於表達框的方式來達到這一目的	the only way to prove these theories is to construct a chromosome with these genes , and we have to do that with framework .
我們發現大片段精確合成dna是非常非常困難的	and what we found was that extraordinary segments of dna are very , very hard .
我的同事漢姆•史密斯和克萊德•哈欽森發明了一個讓人振奮的新方法能讓我們在短短兩週時間內合成一個擁有5000個鹼基對的病毒而且在基因序列和生物學特性上都百分百精確	my colleague hanm smith and clyde hutchingson invented an exciting new way to get us to synthesize a virus that has 5 , 000 base pairs in just two weeks , and has 100 percent accuracy in gene sequence and biology .
那是個相當讓人興奮的實驗:我們僅僅把合成的dna片段注進細菌中 , 突然之間dna就開始引導病毒顆粒的合成而病毒反過來殺死了細菌	it was a pretty exciting experiment: we just injected synthetic dna fragments into the bacteria , and suddenly dna started to direct the synthetic particles from the virus , and the virus was in reverse to kill the bacteria .
這並非第一個合成的病毒一年前已有某種脊髓灰質炎病毒被製造了出來但這卻是唯一達到百分之一活性的病毒耗時三年才合成成功	this isn't the first synthetic virus , it was made a year ago , it was made out of some spinal cord inflammatory virus , but it was the only virus that reached one in three years that was successful .
這是phix-174結構的一個動畫	this is an animation of the phix 1744 structure .

有人立即開始擔心生物武器的威脅不久前我也在參議院委員會和另一個由美國政府成立旨在評價這一領域的特殊委員會上作證	someone immediately started worrying about the threat of biological weapons , and i was there not long ago at the senate committee and at a special committee on the u . s . government .
我認為最重要的是將事實牢記在心而非人們對事情發生的想象	i think it's important to keep facts in mind and not ideology of what's going on .
基本上 , 任何現在已經被測序的病毒其基因組都可以被合成	basically , any virus that's being sequenced at the moment can be synthesized in its genome .
人們立馬被埃博拉病毒或天花病毒之類等嚇壞了但從這些生物體中提取的dna並不具有感染力	people were immediately frightened by things like ebola or smallpox , but the dna that they extracted from these organisms was not infectious .
因此即使有人制成了天花病毒基因組其dna本身並不會引發感染	so even if you manufactured smallpox genomics , the dna itself wouldn't cause infection .
安全部門真正需要擔心的是 " 設計者病毒 "	the security sector really needs to worry about " designer virus . "
只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯曾經花大力氣致力於生物武器的研製	there are only two nations , the u . s . and the former soviet union , working hard on biological weapons .
如果這些研究真的已經終止那麼在未來人為製造出設計者病毒的機率微乎其微	and if these studies have really ended , then the probability of making designer viruses in the future is very subtle .
我想兩年內製造出單細胞生物是可能的	i think singlecelled organisms are possible in two years .
而真核細胞我們自己擁有的這種細胞也可能在十年內製造出來	and the u . nuclear cells that we have can be built within a decade .
我們可以區分開進入這個人工基因組的不同表達框和不同基因使得我們能構建數十種不同的結構	we can distinguish into the different frames and different genes of the artificial genome that allow us to construct dozens of different structures .
關鍵是 , 如何把所有其他的放進來 ?	the key thing is , how do you put all the others in there ?
我們從這些片段開始然後透過一個同源重組系統將其組合到染色體中	we start with these clips , and we reassemble them through a homophobia system into a chromosome .
這來自一種名為耐輻射奇異球菌的生物能在三百萬拉德的輻射劑量下保持活力	this comes from an organism called deinococcus radiodurans that remain vital to three million rads of radiation doses .
在暴露輻射約12到24小時其染色體幾乎完全破碎的情況下它還能將自身的染色體重新組裝起來	in exposure to radiation for about 12 to 24 hours , the chromosome was virtually broken , and it could reassemble the chromosome itself .
這種生物在地球上幾乎無處不在甚至由於人類的活動它們還可能在外太空活動	this organism is virtually everywhere on earth , and because of human activity , they're probably active in space .

這是實際的情形上面是經過170萬拉德輻射之後的染色體	this is the actual scenario: it's a chromosome 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .
幾乎已經支離破碎	it's almost broken .
下面是24小時之後同樣的dna自動重組的結果	here are the same dna automatically reconstructed after 24 hours .
這些生物能做到的真是歎為觀止 。 如果不是數以萬計的話也許我們還能找到數以千計的物種也同樣能夠做到	what all these organisms can do is it's extraordinary to see that , if it's not tens of thousands , maybe we'll find thousands of other species that can do it as well .
這些基因組合成之後第一步就是將它們移植到另一個沒有基因組的細胞中	the first step in these genomes is to transplant them into another cell without a genome .
因此我們認為合成細胞將具有巨大的前景不僅僅在生物學基礎的理解上而且很可能幫我們應對環境和社會問題	so we think that synthetic cells will have huge prospects , not just in biology , but they're very likely to help us respond to environmental and social problems .
例如 , 從我們測序的第三種生物詹氏甲烷球菌 , 生活在相當於水沸點的高溫中以氫作為能量來源並依靠捕獲環境中的二氧化碳為自己提供所需的碳	for example , from the third species that we sequenced , methane bacteria lived at high temperatures the boiling hour and used hydrogen as a source for carbon dioxide to capture the environment and provided itself with carbon dioxide .
由此可知 , 透過大量不同的途徑數以千計的生物能夠捕獲並依賴二氧化碳生存	so you know , through a vast array of different ways , thousands of organisms are capable of capturing and depending on co2 .
因此我們可以透過捕獲大氣中的碳製造生物高聚物或其他產品來替代從石油中工業合成的碳製品	so we can replace this carbon from the oil industry by capturing carbon from the atmosphere , or some other products from polymers and other products .

同樣 , 還有許多途徑能夠用來轉化甲烷	similarly , there are many ways to translate methane .
杜邦公司和挪威石油公司有一大型專案就是把挪威油氣田中的甲烷轉化為有用的產品	one of the biggest programs for dupont and norway was to translate methane from norway into a useful product .
我突然想到 , 將有一個新的領域 " 組合基因組學 " 很快就要誕生因為有了這些新的合成方法有了這麼龐大的基因序列和同源重組我們可以設計出一個能夠每天生產近百萬個染色體的機器人	and it occurred to me that there was a new field called combinator genomics , which was about to be created quickly , because with these new synthesis , we had these huge synthetic genomic sequences and these same reconfigurations , and we could design a robot that could produce a million chromosomes a day .
因此 , 所有的生物學特徵都能透過螢幕來選擇無論是製造氫化學合成 , 或者僅僅是生存能力	so , all biological features can be chosen by screen , whether it's generating hydrogen synthesis or just the ability to live .
理解這些基因的功能將變得觸手可及	and to understand how these genes are functioning , they're going to be tactile .
我們正嘗試改進光合作用以直接在陽光下製造出氫	we're trying to improve photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly in the sun .
光合作用受氧調節而我們使用的對氧不敏感的氫化酶將完全改變這一過程	photosynthesis uses oxygen modulation , and the unsensitive hydrogenase we use will completely change this process .
我們還整合了多種纖維素酶這些酶可以把複雜的糖類分解為簡單的糖類並在同一個細胞內發酵產生酒精	we also integrated multiple cellulose enzymes , enzymes that could break down complex sugars into simple sugars and create alcohol within the same cell .
在一些大型的實驗室裡已經開始利用微生物進行藥品生產	in some of the big labs , we're already starting to make pharmaceutical products with microbes .
環境中化合物的化學比我們最好的化學家制造出來的化合物還要複雜很多	the chemistry of compounds in the environment is much more complex than our best chemists have ever built .
也許未來的工程物種將成為我們的食物來源能量來源環境補救手段甚至取代石化行業	perhaps future engineering species will become our food sources , environmental remedies and even petrochemical industries .
最後讓我以道德和政策上的研究結束吧	let me finish with morality and policy research .
我們推遲了1999年開始的實驗直到對是否應該嘗試製造人工物種這一問題進行了一年半的生物倫理學討論後實驗才繼續進行	and we late , 1999 , and we launched our experiments , until we got to the question of creating artificial species , and it took about a year and a half of bioethical discussion to continue .
每個主要宗教都參與其中	every major religion participates .
真是一項奇怪的研究因為許多宗教領袖都以他們的教義、經文作為法律而且不能從中找出禁止製造生命的條文所以這應該沒什麼問題最根本的擔憂來自生物武器方面但只有開始進行這些實驗之後我們才能找出從事這一切的原因	and it's really a strange study , because many religious leaders are using their textbooks , their scriptures , and they're unable to find those essential worries about creating life , so that's probably the most fundamental concern that we have to worry about biological weapons , but it's only when we do these experiments , so that we can identify what's going on .
目前斯隆基金會已經資助了一個相關的多機構參與的研究以確定這些實驗給社會帶來的風險和益處同時也為像我們這樣的科學團隊在這一領域開展研究制定規則在前進的同時我們也努力成為一個良好的榜樣	the sloan foundation has funded a multiinstitutional study to make sure that these experiments are risks and benefits to society , and that they're also building the rules for the scientific community that we're working on , and we're working on becoming a good role model .
有許多複雜的議題	there's a lot of complex issues .
除了生物恐怖主義它們其實都很簡單:我們能否設計出生產清潔能源的工具透過各種不同的簡單步驟或能徹底改變發展中國家的能源生產模式	beyond bioterrorism , they're actually very simple: we can engineer the tools to make clean energy through a variety of simple steps , or fundamentally changing energy production models in developing countries .

西蒙•斯涅克用一個簡單但是震撼的模型來闡釋激勵人心的領袖力 , 這個模型的核心是一個 " 黃金 " 圓圈 , 意思是領袖素質的根本來源是回答 " 為什麼 ? " 。 他列舉了蘋果公司、馬丁•路德•金還有萊特兄弟成功的例子 , 同時以蒂沃數碼錄影機為失敗的典型 。 雖然蒂沃最近打贏一場官司 , 使得其股價上漲了3倍 , 但是它仍在掙扎中 。	simon sneaker uses a simple but shocking model to illustrate the inspiring leadership , which is at the heart of a golden circle , which means that the leader's essential quality is , " why ? " he served the apple company , martin luther king and the wright brothers ascribing and the outcome of digital digital video , while winning the boss , which has recently been winning the price of the stock .
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye , it's a graham , entrepreneur cracking , sales , selling , success .
西蒙•斯涅克:偉大的領袖如何激勵行動	simon stenke: how inspired great leaders to activate their movements .
當事情的發展出乎意料之外的時候 , 你怎麼解釋 ?	what do you say when things aren't surprising ?
換句話說 , 當別人似乎出乎意料地取得成功的時候 , 你怎麼解釋 ?	in other words , what do you mean when someone seems to have an unexpected success ?
比如說 , 為什麼蘋果公司創新能力這麼強 ?	for example , why do apples be so innovative ?
這麼多年來 , 年復一年 , 他們比所有競爭對手都更加具有創新性 。	over the years , year after year , they've become much more innovative than all competitors .
而其實他們只是一家電腦公司 。	and they're really just a computer company .
他們跟其他公司沒有任何分別 ,	they're not distinguished from any other company .
有同樣的途徑 , 接觸到同樣的人才 , 同樣的代理商 , 顧問 , 和媒體 。	there's the same approach , the same talent , the same proxies , consultants and media .
那為什麼他們就似乎有那麼一點不同尋常呢 ?	so why do they seem a little bit different ?
同樣的 , 為什麼是由馬丁•路德•金來領導民權運動 ?	similarly , why a civil rights movement , martin luther king ?
那個時候在美國 , 民權運動之前 , 不僅僅只有他一個人飽受歧視 。 他也決不是那個時代唯一的偉大演說家 。	at the time , before the civil rights movement , it wasn't just about him that he was upset by discrimination , it wasn't the only great orator of that era .
又為什麼懷特兄弟能夠造出動力控制的載人飛機 , 跟他們相比 , 當時的其他團隊似乎更有能力 , 更有資金 ,	and why the white brothers were able to build mobile maneuverable airplanes compared to them , other groups seemed to have more ability , more funding than others at the time .
他們卻沒能製造出載人飛機 , 懷特兄弟打敗了他們 。	they didn't make loading airplanes , and the white brothers beat them .
一定還有一些什麼別的因素在起作用 。	there must be something else that works .
大概三年半之前 , 我有了個新發現 ,	about three and a half years ago , i discovered something new .
這個發現完全改變了我對這個世界如何運作的看法 。 甚至從根本上改變了我的工作生活方式 。	it completely changed the way i think about how the world works , and fundamentally changed the way i work in my work life .
那就是我發現了一種模式 ,	and that's how i found a pattern .
我發現世界上所有偉大的令人振奮的領袖和組織 , 無論是蘋果公司、馬丁•路德•金還是懷特兄弟 , 他們思考、行動、交流溝通的方式都完全一樣 ,	i found out that all the great , exciting leaders and organizations in the world , apple , martin luther king and the white brothers , think , do and communicate in exactly the same way .
但是跟所有其他人的方式完全相反 。	but the opposite is true for everyone else .
我所做的僅僅是把它整理出來 。 這可能是世上最簡單的概念 。	all i'm doing is tidying it out , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .
我稱它為黃金圓環 。	i call it the golden circle .
為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 是什麼 ?	why ? what ?
這小小的模型就解釋了為什麼一些組織和領導者能夠在別人不能的地方激發出靈感和潛力 。	this little model explains why some organizations and leaders can inspire and potential where others can't .
我來儘快地解釋一下這些術語 。	let me explain the terms as quickly as i can .
地球上的每個人 , 每個組織都明白自己做的是什麼 , 百分之百 。	every single person on the planet understands what they're doing , 100 percent .
其中一些知道該怎麼做 , 你可以稱之為是你的差異價值 , 或是你的獨特工藝 , 或是你的獨特賣點也好 , 怎麼說都行 。	some of them know what to do , you might call it your differences , or your unique craftsmanship , or your unique selling points , or whatever it is .
但是非常 , 非常少的人和組織明白為什麼做 。	but very , very few people and organizations know why .
這裡的 " 為什麼 " 和 " 為利潤 " 沒有關係 ,	the " why " and " profit " doesn't matter .
利潤只是一個結果 , 永遠只能是一個結果 。	the profits are only a single outcome , always a single outcome .
我說的 " 為什麼 " 指的是:你的目的是什麼 ?	and by " why " i mean: what is your purpose ?
你這樣做的原因是什麼 ? 你懷著什麼樣的信念 ?	what makes you do that ? what kind of faith are you preserving ?
你的機構為什麼而存在 ?	why do your institutions exist ?
你每天早上是為什麼而起床 ?	why do you wake up every morning ?
為什麼別人要在乎你 ?	why should anyone care about you ?
結果是 , 我們思考的方式 , 行動的方式 , 交流的方式都是由外向內的 。	it turns out that the way we think , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is by extroverts .
很顯然的 , 我們所採用的方式是從清晰開始 , 然後到模糊的東西 。	obviously , what we do is we start with clarity , and we go to fuzzy stuff .
但是激勵型領袖以及組織機構 , 無論他們的規模大小 , 所在領域 , 他們思考 , 行動和交流的方式都是從裡向外的 。	but the inspiring leaders and organizations , both in their scale and in their area , are thinking and doing and communicating from inside out .
舉個例子吧 。	let me give you an example .
我舉蘋果公司是因為這個例子簡單易懂 , 每個人都能理解 。	i'm the apple company because it's easy to understand , everybody understands .
如果蘋果公司跟其他公司一樣 , 他們的市場營銷資訊就會是這個樣子: " 我們做最棒的電腦 ,	if apple were the same as any other company , their marketing information would look like this: " we make the best computers .
設計精美 , 使用簡單 , 介面友好 。	design elaborates , using simple , friendly interfaces .
你想買一臺嗎 ? " 不怎麼樣吧 。	you want to buy one ? " not so much .
這就是我們大多數人的交流方式 ,	that's how most of us communicate .
也是大多數市場推廣的方式 , 大部分銷售所採用的方式 , 也是我們大部分人互相交流的方式 。	it's also the way most markets broadcast , the way most sales are adopted , and it's the way most of us talk to each other .
我們說我們的職業是幹什麼的 , 我們說我們是如何的與眾不同 , 或者我們怎麼比其他人更好 , 然後我們就期待著一些別人的反應 , 比如購買 , 比如投票 , 諸如此類 。	we say what our professions do , we say how we're specialized , or how we're better than others , and then we expect people to react , like , purchase , like voting , and so on .
這是我們新開的的律師事務所 , 我們擁有最棒的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是能滿足客戶的要求 。	it's our new law firm , our best lawyers and our biggest clients , and we're always fulfilling the customers' demands .
這是我們的新車型 , 非常省油 , 真皮座椅 。 買一輛吧 。	this is our new vehicle , very fuelefficient , derriet seat . get one .
這是蘋果公司實際上的溝通方式:	this is how apple actually communicates .
" 我們做的每一件事情 , 都是為了突破和創新 。	" everything we do to break it down and to innovate .
我們堅信應該以不同的方式思考 。	we firmly believe that we should think differently .
我們挑戰現狀的方式是透過把我們的產品設計得十分精美 , 使用簡單 , 和介面友好 。	the way we challenge the status quo is by designing our products perfectly beautifully , using simple , interface friendly .
我們只是在這個過程中做出了最棒的電腦 。	we're just making the best computers out of this process .
想買一臺嗎 ? "	want to buy one ? "
感覺完全不一樣 , 對吧 ? 你已經準備從我這裡買一臺了 。	feel completely different , right ? you're ready to buy one from me .
我所做的只是將傳遞資訊的順序顛倒一下而已 。	all i'm doing is turning the sequence upside down the sequence of information .
事實已經向我們證明 , 人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念和宗旨 。	it's been shown to us that people are not buying products that you make , and people are buying your beliefs and missions .
人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念 。	people don't buy products that you make ; people buy your beliefs .
這就解釋了為什麼這裡的每個人從蘋果公司買電腦時都覺得理所當然 。	which explains why everyone here takes it for granted when they're buying a computer from apple .
但是我們從蘋果公司買mp3播放器 , 手機 , 或者數碼攝像機時 , 也感覺很舒服 。	but we bought an mp3 player from an apple company , or a digital camera , and it was really comfortable .
而其實 , 我剛才已經說過 , 蘋果公司只是個電腦公司 。	and in fact , as i said , apple's just a computer company .
沒有什麼能從結構上將蘋果公司同競爭對手區分開來 。	there's nothing that separates the competitors from the structure of the apple company .
競爭對手和蘋果公司有同樣的能力製造所有這些產品 。	competitors like apple have the same capacity to make all of these products .
實際上 , 他們也嘗試過 。	in fact , they've tried .
幾年前 , 捷威公司推出了平板電視 。	a few years ago , the fastwell company introduced flatscreen tvs .
他們製造平板電視的能力很強 ,	they're very capable of making flatscreen tvs .
因為他們做平板顯示器已經很多年了 。	because they've been working on the tablets for years .
戴爾公司推出了mp3播放器和掌上電腦 , 他們產品的質量非常好 , 產品的設計也非常不錯 。 但是也沒有人買他們的這些產品 。	the daler introduced an mp3 player and the palmpilot , and the mass of their products is very , very nice , and nobody bought them .
其實 , 說到這裡 , 我們無法想象會從戴爾公司買mp3播放器 。	well , speaking of this , we can't imagine buying mp3 players from the dell company .
你為什麼會從一家電腦公司買mp3播放器呢 ?	why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?
但是每天我們都這麼做 。	but we do it every day .
人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念 。	people don't buy products that you make ; people buy your beliefs .
做公司的目標不是要跟所有需要你的產品的人做生意 ,	it's not about commercializing with everyone who needs your product .
而是跟與你有著相同理念的人做生意 。	it's about recommending business with people who have ideas with you .
這是最精彩的部分 。 我說的這些沒有一個是我自己的觀點 。	it's the best part . none of these things , i'm talking about , are my opinions .
這些觀點都能從生物學裡面找到根源 。	these ideas can be found in biology .
不是心理學 , 是生物學 。	it's not psychology , it's biology .
當你俯視看大腦的橫截面 , 你會發現人類大腦實際上分成三個主要部分 , 而這三個主要部分和黃金圓環匹配得非常好 。	when you look at the crosssection of the brain , you'll see that the human brain actually has three key components , and those three main components are very well matched with golden circles .
我們最新的腦部 , 管轄智力的腦部 , 或者說我們的大腦皮層 , 對應著 " 是什麼 " 這個圓環 。	our newest brain , the jurisdictional brain , or our cerebral cortex , corresponds to what the circle is .
大腦皮層負責我們所有的理性和邏輯的思考和語言功能 。	the cerebral cortex is responsible for all of our rational thinking and logical thinking .
中間的兩個部分是我們的兩個邊腦 。 邊腦負責我們所有的情感 , 比如信任和忠誠 ,	the two parts in the middle are our two sides of our brains , and our brains are responsible for all of our emotions , like trust and loyalty .
也負責所有的行為和決策 , 但這部分沒有語言功能 。	it's also responsible for all kinds of behaviors and decisions , but that doesn't have language features .
換句話說 , 當我們由外向內交流時 , 沒錯 , 人們可以理解大量的複雜資訊 , 比如特徵 , 優點 , 事實和圖表 。	in other words , when we communicate inwards , yes , people can understand lots of complex information like features , privilege , facts and diagrams .
但不足以激發行動 。	but it wasn't enough to activate action .
當我們由內向外交流時 , 我們是在直接同控制行為的那一部分大腦對話 , 然後我們由人們理性地思考我們所說和做的事情 。	when we're introverts , we're talking to the part of the brain that is directly controlling behavior , and then we're rationally thinking about what we're saying and what we're doing .
這就是那些發自內心的決定的來源 。	and that's where the internal decisions come from .
你知道 , 有時候你展示給一些人所有的資料圖表 , 他們會說 " 我知道這些資料和圖表是什麼意思 , 但就是感覺不對 。 "	you know , sometimes you show all the data graphs to some people , and they say , " i know what this data and graph means , but it just feels wrong . "
為什麼我們會用這個動詞 , " 感覺 " 不對 ?	why do we use this verb , " feel , " right ?
因為控制決策的那一部分大腦並不支配語言 ,	because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking is not in control of language .
我們只好說 " 我不知道為什麼 , 就是感覺不對 。 "	and we said , " i don't know why , but it just doesn't feel right . "
或者有些時候 , 你說聽從心的召喚 , 或者說聽從靈魂 。	or there's a time when you're talking to the cause , or you're listening to the soul .
我不想把這些觀念分解得太徹底 , 但心和靈魂都不是控制行為的部分 。	i don't want to break these ideas down too thoroughly , but the heart and soul are not a part of the behavior .
所有這一切都發生在你的邊腦 , 控制決策行為而非語言的邊腦 。	all of this is happening at your side of the brain , controlling decisionmaking behavior rather than language .
如果你自己都不知道你為什麼幹你所做的事情 , 而別人要對你的動機作出反應 , 那麼你怎麼可能贏得大家對你的支援 , 從你這裡購買東西 , 或者 , 更重要的 , 對你忠誠並且想成為你正在做的事情的一分子呢 ?	if you don't know why you do what you do , and others react to your motivation , then how can you win people's support from you , buying things from you , or , more importantly , loyalty to you and want to be part of what you're doing ?
再說一次 , 目標不僅僅是將你有的東西賣給需要它們的人 ; 而是將東西賣給跟你有共同信念的人 。	again , the goal is to sell not just what you have , but to the people who need it to you , but to the people who share your beliefs .
目標不僅僅是僱傭那些需要一份工作的人 ; 目標是僱傭那些同你有共同信念的人 。	the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; the goal is to employ people who share your faith .
你知道嗎 , 我總是說 , 如果你僱傭某人只是因為他能做這份工作 , 他們就只是為你開的工資而工作 , 但是如果你僱傭跟你有共同信念的人 , 他們會為你付出熱血 , 汗水和淚水 。	you know , i always say that if you hire someone for this work , they're just working for the wages that you have , but if you hire people that share your faith , they give you bleeding , sweat and tears .
這一點 , 沒有比懷特兄弟的故事更恰當的例子了 。	now , there's no more appropriate example of the story than the white brothers .
大多數人都沒聽說過塞繆爾•蘭利這個人 。	now , most people haven't heard of this guy , semuri lonley .
20世紀初期 , 投入機動飛行器的熱情就像當今的網站熱 ,	in the early 20th century , the passion to put on aircraft was like hot websites today .
每個人都在做嘗試 。	everyone was trying .
塞繆爾•蘭利擁有所有大家認為是成功的要素 。	cerme langley has all the things that people think are successful .
我的意思是 , 即便是現在 , 你問別人 " 為什麼你的產品或者公司失敗了呢 ? "	i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or your company fail ? "
人們總是用同樣的三個東西以同樣的排列順序來回答你 , 缺乏資金 , 用人不善 , 形勢不好 。	people are always responding to you in the same three arrangement in the same order , lack of funding , lack of funding , lack of adversity , not in the good shape .
總是那三種理由 , 所以讓我們來逐個分析一下 。	and there are three reasons why , so let's go through this .
國防部給了塞繆爾•蘭利5萬美金作為研製飛行器的資金 。	the department of defense gave samuel lang 50 , 000 dollars to a construction machine .
所以說 , 資金不是問題 。	so , funding is not the problem .
他在哈佛大學工作過 , 也在史密森尼學會工作過 , 人脈極其廣泛 。 他認識當時最優秀的人才 。	he's worked at harvard university , he's worked at the smithsonian , he's been widely connected to the best people at the time .
因此 , 他僱傭了用資金能吸引到的最優秀的人才 。 當時的市場形勢相當有利 。	so he employed the best people who funded the most to attract the brilliant market capital .
紐約時報對他做跟蹤報道 , 每個人都支援他 。	the new york times wrote about him and stalked about him , and everybody supported him .
但是為什麼你們連聽都沒聽說過他呢 ?	but why haven't you heard about him ?
與此同時 , 幾百公里之外的俄亥俄州代頓市有一對兄弟 , 奧維爾•萊特和維爾伯•萊特 , 他們倆沒有任何我們認為的成功的要素 。	and meanwhile , hundreds of kilometers away in ohio city , there's a pair of brothers , orville and wilbur wright , who doesn't have the ingredients that we think are successful .
他們沒有錢 。 他們用腳踏車店的收入來追求他們的夢想 。 萊特兄弟的團隊中沒有一個人上過大學 , 就連奧維爾和維爾伯也沒有 。 紐約時報更是不沾邊的 。	they had no money . they pursued their dream with a bicycle revenue . none of the wright brothers had ever been to college , and none of them had ever even been to college orville and the new york times were just struck .
不同的是 , 奧維爾和維爾伯追求的是一個事業 , 一個目標 , 一種信念 。	what's different is that what orville and wilbur are looking for is a career , a purpose , a belief .
他們相信如果他們能研製出飛行器 , 將會改變全世界的發展程序 。	they believed that if they could develop vehicles that would change the course of the world .
塞繆爾•蘭利就不同了 ,	semuri lanley was a different one .
他想要發財 , 他想要成名 。	he wanted to finance , and he wanted to become famous .
他追求的是最終結果 ,	he pursued the end result .
是變得富有 。	it's becoming rich .
看吧 , 看接下來怎麼樣了 。	see what happens next ?
那些懷有和懷特兄弟一樣夢想的人跟他們一起熱血朝天地奮鬥著 。	people who dream like the white brothers , they struggle with their heat .
另一邊的人則是為了工資而工作 。	the other side was working for wages .
後來流傳的故事說 , 每次懷特兄弟出去實驗時 , 都必須帶著五組零件 , 因為那是在他們回來吃晚飯之前將要墜毀的次數 。	the later story goes that every time the white brothers went out to experiment , they had to carry five pieces , because that's the number of times they would crash before they return to dinner .
最後 , 在1903年12月17日 , 懷特兄弟成功起飛 , 但是當時沒有任何其他人在場目睹 。	and finally , on december 17 , 1903 , the white brothers took off , but nobody else was there .
我們是在幾天後才知道的 。	we didn't know it until a few days later .
後來的事情進一步證實了蘭利動機不純 , 他在懷特兄弟成功的當天就辭職了 。	what happened further confirmed that langley motivation was not pure , and he resigned success on the day of the white brothers .
他本來應該可以說: " 夥計們 , 這真是一項偉大的發明 , 我可以改進你們的技術 。 " 但是他沒有 ,	he should have said , " guys , this is a great invention , and i can improve your technology , " but he doesn't .
因為他不是第一個製造出飛機的人 , 他就不會變得富有 , 他也不會變得有名 , 所以他辭職了 。	because he wasn't the first person to make an airplane , he wouldn't be rich , and he wouldn't become famous , so he quit .
人們買的不是你的產品 ; 而是你的信念 。	people are not buying your product ; they buy your beliefs .
如果你講述你的信念 , 你將吸引那些跟你擁有同樣信念的人 。	if you talk about your beliefs , you will attract people who share your beliefs .
但是為什麼吸引那些跟你擁有同樣信念的人非常重要呢 ?	but why is it so important to attract people who have the same beliefs as you ?
創新的傳播有一個規律 , 如果你不知道這個規律 , 你一定了解這個概念 。	there's a pattern in the spread of innovation , and if you don't know the pattern , you've got to understand it .
我們的社會中 , 有2.5%的人是革新者 。	two and a half percent of our society are revolutionaries .
13.5%的人是早期的少部分採納者 。	thirteen and a half percent of the people were a small segment of the early days .
接下來的34%是早期接受的大多數 , 然後是比較晚接受的大多數和最後行動的 。	over the next 34 percent are early accepting quarters , and then a much later accepts most and last actions .
這部分最後行動的人買按鍵電話的唯一原因是因為他們再也買不到轉盤電話了 。	and the only reason that the people who ended up buying their phones was because they couldn't buy a transplant phone anymore .
雖然我們在不同的時候會處在這個曲線上不同的位置 , 但是創新的傳播規律告訴我們如果你想在大眾市場上獲得成功 , 或者要大眾接納一個點子 , 你得等到獲得15%-18%的市場接受度這個轉折點之後才行 。 那時之後市場才真正開啟 。	and although we're all different at different times , the distribution of innovations tells us that if you want to succeed in the public market or to embrace an idea , you have to wait for 15 to 18 percent of the market receiving points at that point , and that's when the market really started .
我喜歡問公司: " 你的新生意怎麼樣呀 ? "	i like to ask a company , " what about your new business ? "
他們會很自豪地告訴你 " 哦 , 大概有10%吧 。 "	they'll tell you proudly , " oh , it's about 10 percent . "
是呀 , 你有可能就在10%的顧客群這裡過不去了 。	yeah , you're probably right here in 10 percent of the customers .
我們都能讓10%的人 " 意會 " ,	we can all get 10 percent of the people in " consciousness . "
對 , 我們一般這樣形容他們 。	yeah , that's how we generally describe them .
就好比描述那種感覺: " 哦 , 他們有點心領神會了 " 。	it's like describing that feeling , " oh , they're kind of getting the lord god out . "
問題是:你怎麼在他們還沒有成為你的顧客之前就發現那些能意會的人 , 和那些不能意會的人 ?	the question is: how did you find someone who didn't have the consciousness of your customers before they were there ?
這就是問題的所在 , 就是這點間隙 , 你得把這個間隙給填上 , 正如傑弗裡穆爾所說的 , " 跨越鴻溝 " 。 因為早期的大多數不會嘗試新事物 , 除非有些人已經先嚐試過了 。	so that's the problem , and that's the gap , and you need to fill it in , and as geoffrey muir talked about , because most early on it isn't trying new things unless some of you have tried it before .
而這些人 , 創新者和早期的少數人 , 他們喜歡大膽的嘗試 。	and these people , the innovators and the early minorities , they love audacious endeavor .
他們更自然地憑直覺做事情 , 發自於他們的世界觀的直覺 , 而不僅僅是因為市場上有什麼樣的產品 。	they're more naturally doing things with their intuitions , coming from their worldview instincts , not just because of what's there .
這是一批在iphone上市的頭幾天去排隊等六個小時來購買的人 , 而其實只要等一個星期你就可以隨便走進店裡從貨架上買到 。	this was the first people on the iphone queuing for six hours on their iphone , and actually just waited a week , you could just walk into the store and buy it off the shelf .
這是一批在平板電視剛推出時會花4萬美金買一臺的人 , 儘管當時的技術還不成熟 。	this is a group of people that , when the tablet was launched , it cost 40 , 000 dollars to buy one , despite the fact that the techniques weren't ready .
補充說一下 , 他們並不是因為技術的先進而買那些產品 , 而是為了他們自己 。	and to put that in context , they're not buying those products because of the advancement of technology , but because of it .
因為他們想成為第一個體驗新產品的人 。	because they want to be the first one to experience a new product .

你是如何回憶起將車停在了什麼地方呢 ? 你怎麼判斷自己是否走對了方向呢 ? 神經系統科學家尼爾•伯吉斯研究了神經系統的定位功能原理 , 以及該原理與記憶和想象的關係 。	how do you recall where the car is parked in ? how do you determine whether you're on the right direction ? neil bergius is studying the locations of the nervous system , and the relationship between the principle and the memory and the imagination .
brain , cognitivescience , exploration , neuroscience , science	if you look at it , there's cognitives , there's pacemake , there .
尼爾•伯吉斯:大腦是怎樣幫我們定位的	niel bergis: how does the brain help us position ?
當我們在大型停車場停車後 , 如何回憶起將車停在了哪個車位呢 ?	when we parked in a big parking lot , how do we recall where we've parked our car ?
這就是現在困擾荷馬的問題 。	so that's the problem of the horse .
接下來我們將嘗試瞭解此時他腦中正開展何種 " 運動 " 。	and then we're going to try to understand what exercise is going on in his brain right now .
我們先著眼於大腦海馬區 , 即黃色的區域這是我們的記憶器官 。	we're going to focus on the hippocampus , the yellow area , which is our memory organ .
如果海馬區出現損傷 , 像老年痴呆症患者一樣 , 你將喪失記憶力 , 乃至記不起將車停在了何處 。	if you have damage to the hippocampus , like someone with advanced alzheimer's , you're going to lose your memory and remember where the car is parked .
hippocampus這個詞源自拉丁語 , 有 " 海馬 " 之意因為腦中海馬區的形狀看上去有點像 " 海馬 " 。	the hippocampus comes from the latin word " hippocampus " because it looks a little bit like " seahorse " in the hippocampus .
海馬區和大腦其它區域的組成相似 , 都由神經元構成 。	the hippocampus , similar to the rest of the brain , is made of neurons .
人的大腦由大約一千億個神經元細胞組成 。	the human brain consists of about 100 billion neurons .
每個神經元細胞之間透過一些連線中介互相傳送小的電脈衝或者尖峰電壓來進行 " 交流 " 。	each neuron is communicating with each other via some interconnected pulses or spike pressure .
海馬區由兩層片狀的細胞群構成 , 這兩層細胞群緊密相連 。	the hippocampus is composed of two layers of cells that are intimately connected .
科學家們透過記錄老鼠在某環境中搜羅食物時其腦中單個神經元細胞的反應來了解 " 空間記憶 " 的工作原理與工作機制 。	scientists respond by recording how a single neuron in the brain responds to memory works and works in a particular environment .
現在想象一下 , 我們正在為這隻老鼠的海馬區中的一個神經元細胞 " 錄影 " 。	now imagine that we are videoing a neuron in the hippocampus of this mouse .
每當這個細胞發出小型尖峰電壓 , 隨後會出現一個紅點以及咔噠的一聲 。	whenever this cell produces a small , spikey pressure , a red dot and a click appears .
我們可以看出每當老鼠進入環境中某一特定位置 , 這個神經元細胞便會有反應 。	and we can see that every time a mouse enters a certain location in the environment , that neuron will respond .
然後這個細胞再透過小型尖峰電壓將以上資訊傳遞給大腦的其它區域 。	and this cell , again , sends that information to other areas of the brain via small peak pressure .
這麼一來 , 我們可以憑藉這個細胞傳送訊號的頻率推知老鼠經過的相應位置 。	this way , we can extrapolate where mice have according to the frequency of this cell .
倘若我們記錄的是很多不同的神經元細胞 , 就會發現當老鼠處於不同的位置上時 , 不同的神經元細胞會產生各自的電訊號 , 正如我們在這些方形中看到的那樣 。	if we record a lot of different neurons , we'll see that when rats are in different positions , different neurons will produce their own electrical signals , just like we see in these squares .
這些訊號為大腦中的其它區域勾勒出一張地圖 , 持續地向大腦指示出 , " 我現在位於環境中的哪個具體點上 ? "	these signals draw a map of the other regions of the brain constantly instructing the brain , " where am i in the environment ? "
我們也記錄人腦中的 " 定位神經元細胞 " 。	we also documented the targeted neurons in the human brain .
癲癇病患者有時需要監測他們的腦電活動情況 。	people with epilepsy sometimes need to monitor their electrical activity .
一些患者玩一種電子遊戲 , 遊戲中他們在一個小鎮上自由開車 。	some people played an video game where they were driving in a small town .
然後當他們驅車駛過鎮上的某一處時 , 他們大腦海馬區中的 " 定位神經元細胞 " 便會被啟用 , 發出訊號 。	and when they drive over town somewhere in the town , the location neuron cells in the hippocampus are then turned on and off the signal .
那麼這 " 定位細胞 " 是怎麼知道老鼠或人處於某個位置的呢 ?	so how does a positioning cell know that a mouse or a person is in a position ?
這裡有兩個神經元細胞 , 它們告訴我們 , 在定位時環境的邊界是至關重要的 。	so here we have two neurons , and they tell us that the boundaries of the positioning environment are essential .
上面的這個細胞傾向於在老鼠向盒子中部走去時產生訊號 。	the cell up there is a tendency to create a signal as it walks through the box .
因此當你將盒子擴大 , 相應的訊號活躍區也隨之擴大 。	so when you expand the box , it's very active , it expands .
下面的這個喜歡在老鼠緊鄰南面屏障時作出反應 。	the one at the bottom responds when it hits a south barrier .
因此當你在盒中放入另一屏障時 , 不論老鼠在盒中何處 , 只要它的南面有屏障 , 該細胞中的相應位置便會同時產生訊號 。	so when you put a barrier in a box , wherever a mouse is in a box , there's barrier in it , and the position of that response in it will produce a signal simultaneously .
這表明瞭解到達邊界比如周邊的建築物等需要的距離和方向對於海馬區的 " 工作 " 而言至關重要 。	this suggests that the distance and the direction of distance and direction of buildings to the neighborhood is crucial to the hippocampus .
而且確實 , 在老鼠蒐羅環境時 , 我們在海馬區的輸入訊號中 , 檢測到能對距環境邊界的特定距離與方向作出精確感應的神經元細胞 。	and indeed , in the mice that gathered the input signal in the hippocampus , we detected specific distances and directions in the environment .
這裡左邊的細胞 , 你可以看出 , 當老鼠向東靠近邊界或屏障時 , 該細胞都會作出反應 , 不論這邊界是一個方盒的邊還是一個圓柱盒的邊甚至是老鼠繞著轉的桌布的垂簾 。	the cell on the left , you can see , as it goes towards the border or barrier of the east , the cell reacts , whether it's the side of a box or whether it's a cylinder box or even a tableclosed curtain .
而右面的細胞則是在老鼠南面出現邊界時響應 , 不論這邊界是桌布的垂簾還是一堵牆甚至是兩個被隔開的桌子之間的間隙 。	and the cell on the right responds to the border south of the mouse , regardless of whether it's the tableclothing curtain or whether it's a wall or even a gap between two separate tables .
以上是我們所推測的一種 " 定位細胞 " 給動物定位的方式 。	so that's one way we've suspected of certain cells for animals .
我們也可檢測 , 人類在簡單環境中 , 是怎樣給諸如這面旗這樣的物體定位的或者乾脆把這物體想成你的車 。	we can also detect how humans , in a simple environment , think of an object like this flag or maybe think of it as your car .
我們先讓人們熟悉一下環境 , 同時記下物體所在的位置 。	we first let people recognize the environment while we're memorizing the location of the object .
接著 , 再讓他們回到那個環境 , 通常他們都能根據記憶準確無誤地標出物體所在的位置 。	and then , when they go back to that environment , they're typically able to mark their locations based on memory accurately .
但在一些試驗中 , 我們會改變環境的形狀和尺度 , 正如我們在 " 定位細胞 " 實驗中所做的那樣 。	but in some trials , we change the shape and size of the environment just as we do in the target cells .
如此 , 我們可以透過研究實驗者改變環境的形狀和尺度 , 來了解旗幟發生了怎樣的位移	so , we can learn by studying the shapes and scales of the environment by changing the shapes and the scales of the flag .
比如現在你所看到的 , 假設這面旗幟在如圖中小四方形內的 " × " 的位置 , 然後接著你問人們小旗在哪 , 但實際上你已經將總環境的尺度擴大了 , 結果他們所認為的旗所在的位置也相應地向外擴張 , 而這擴張的模式和 " 定位細胞 " 的一模一樣 。	so let's say that this flag , if you look at it like the position in those little squares of those four squares , and then you ask people where the flag is , but actually you've expanded the scale of the environment , and what they think is the flag that expands outwards , and the expansion is exactly the same as the position cell .
這就好像你是透過儲存被某一特定位置所激發的 " 定位細胞 " 產生的訊號模式來記憶小旗的位置的 , 接著當你回到那個地點的時候 , 透過四處打量 , 便可以將你當前腦中 " 定位細胞 " 的訊號模式與之前的模式進行匹配 。	it's like a signal pattern that you generate by storing a specific location of cells to memory the flag , and then you come back to that location , and through those previous calendars , you can match the signal patterns of a position cell in your teeth .
這個過程便可讓你回到 " 老地方 " 。	and that allows you to go back to where you are .
我們也能透過位移來給自己定位 。	we can also locate ourselves by giving ourselves bits .
因此當我們外出時或許是我們停車後下來隨便走走我們可以給自己定位 , 因為我們可以粗略地將自己的運動路線與大體的返回方向進行整合 。	so when we're out , maybe we're parking and walking around and we're positioning ourselves , because we can roughly crudely integrate our motion circuits with the body back and forth .
" 定位細胞 " 也能從一種叫做 " 網狀細胞 " 的細胞那兒獲得此類線路整合的資訊 。	" positioning cells " also gets integrated information from a cell called a mesh cell .
目前在向海馬區的訊號輸入中又發現了 " 網狀細胞 " , 它們與 " 定位細胞 " 有點類似 。	now , input into the hippocampus , the signals have come up with net cells , and they're a little bit like the positioning cell .
隨著老鼠的 " 四處探索 " , 每一個神經元細胞被大量各種位置所激發的訊號組合在一起 , 貫穿整個環境構成一個令人驚歎的規整的三角網格 。	as the mouse's " explorations " mice , each neuron is combined with signals inspired by locations of locations and forming an amazingly regular grid throughout the environment .
倘若你對一系列 " 網狀細胞 " 進行記錄這裡以不同的顏色區分每一個細胞發出的訊號都能形成網狀 , 遍及整個環境 , 而且每一個細胞的網狀訊號集的位置都與其他細胞有一定偏差 。	if you document the sequence of net cells in a series of different colors , every signal that emits a mesh , spreads across the environment , and every single cell has a location that is a certain deviation from other cells .
因此紅色標註的細胞訊號集合在這個網格上 , 綠色的是這個 , 而藍色的是這個 。	so the red shown cell signals are gathered on this grid , and the green one is this one , and the blue one is this one .
因此綜合來看 , 這就好像老鼠可以在它所到達的環境中建立一個虛擬的位置訊號網這就有點像你在地圖上所看到的經線和緯線 , 只不過要將線替換成 " 三角形 " 。	so it's a kind of virtual signaling network of rats that are arriving in their environment , kind of like the lines and latitudes you see on the map , except for replacing the lines in triangles .
當老鼠移動的時候 , 這些電訊號能透過這些細胞傳遞給下一個神經元細胞從而為老鼠定位 , 這樣老鼠就能在運動時知道自己身在何處 。	and when it's moving , these electrical signals can pass through these cells to the next neuron in order to locate the mouse , so that the rat can know where it is in the motion .
那麼人類是否有 " 網狀細胞 " 呢 ?	do we have net cells ?
因為所有的網狀訊號集合體都有相同的對稱軸 , 以及相同的網格朝向 , 這裡以橘紅色標識 , 這就意味著大腦中特定部位的所有網狀細胞的聯網行為的變化應該取決於我們是在向著這六個方向運動還是沿著六個方向之間所夾的某一個方向運動 。	because all of the symmetry collections of mesh are the same axes , and the same grid shrinking , shown here in orange , suggesting that the change in the brain of all mesh cells in the brain depends on whether we're moving in one or the other or the other or the other in between or six directions .
我們可以為人們做核磁共振掃描 , 與此同時讓他們玩一個小型電子遊戲 , 還是之前所說的那個遊戲 , 然後來看看當時的訊號 。	we can do mri scans for people , and at the same time , we'll have them play a little video game , or whatever that was called , and then we'll have a look at that signal .
啊哈沒錯 , 你在人腦中的內嗅皮層上看到了網狀細胞 , 而它們出現的位置和老鼠的網狀細胞在大腦中所出現的位置一樣 。	aha , exactly , you see a mesh of cells in the smell of the human brain , and they show up in exactly the same location as the mesh of the rat's mesh in the brain .
現在我們回頭看看荷馬 。	now let's go back to homer .
他可能憑藉與周邊建築以及四周邊界的相對距離和方向來回憶他的車停在哪兒 。	he's probably recalling his memory of where he's parked in relatively distant from the building and the borders around him .
而那將由專門 " 檢測邊界 " 的神經元細胞發出的訊號來執行 。	and that's going to be generated by the signals from the neurons that specialize on the border .
他可能也記得自己是怎麼從停車場走出來的 , 而這就有賴於網狀細胞發出訊號了 。	and he may remember how he came out of a parking lot and it's relying on the signals that net cells are sending out signals .
這兩種型別的神經元細胞都可以啟用 " 定位細胞 " 。	both of these different neurons are activated with " targeted cells . "
因此荷馬成功折返的方法便是在走動中尋求與他之前停車時腦中所建立的訊號集樣式最為匹配的一個腦中即時形成的訊號集樣式 。	so the way homer has successfully returned is a signal episode built in a brain during his previous parking .
而那就能將他領回 " 老地方 " 了 , 這個過程與最終的目標視物無關不論他的車是否還在那兒他都能找到停車點 。	and that gets him back to the " old places , " which is not about the final goal , no matter whether his car is still there , and he can find parking spots .
或許車已經被拖走了 ,	maybe the car has been dragged out .
但他仍然知道車原來停在哪 , 因此他會回到原位去取車 。	but he knew where the vehicle was pull , so he would return to the extract .
撇開 " 空間記憶力 " 而言 , 倘若我們單獨觀察這種網狀訊號集在整個大腦中的活動情況 , 就會發現這種訊號形式分佈廣泛 , 每當我們需要回憶一些自己過去的經歷時這種網狀的訊號形式就會活躍起來 , 譬如 , 當你試圖回憶上次參加婚禮的情況時	and aside from spatial memory , if we were to observe this mesh activity across the brain , this signal was widely distributed , and every time we had to recall some of the experiences of our past , we would have this cyberstric signal activity when you were trying to remember , for example , the last wedding situation .
因此有可能 , 神經元細胞再現空間的功能也參與視覺畫面的呈現這樣當我們試圖回憶一個曾經置身其中的場面時 , 至少可以藉助想象而勾勒出整個場景 。	so it's possible that neurons reclaim the function of space and visualization in such a way that when we try to recall a scene that has been introduced , at least can check the entire scene through the imagination .
倘若事實果真如此 , 記憶的形成就開始於: " 定位細胞 " 透過這些縝密的連結相互啟用然後 " 邊界感應細胞 " 被再次啟用從而形成我們視點周圍的場景的空間格局 。	and if that is true , it begins with a memory formation of a cell , which is available by these carefully interconnected connections , and then the border sensing cells are reshaped in response to a spatial grid that we see around us .
網狀細胞可以使視點穿透那個空間 。	net cells can make your eyes click through that space .
而另一種 " 方位細胞 " , 我之前沒有提到它 , 它們像指南針一樣 , 都是根據你的朝向來作出反應的 。	and then there's another digital cell that i didn't mention before , and they respond like compasses based on what you've been doing .
它們可以明確你需要在腦中形成哪個方位的影象 , 就拿回憶婚禮情景來說 , 以上過程就能讓你回想起那一切 。	they can specifically see which orientation you're going to need to form in your brain , and take a recall of your wedding scenario , and that allows you to recall that .
好了 , 以上就是在認知神經科學領域所開闢的新紀元 , 在這個領域中 , 我們開始嘗試從大腦中數以億計的單個神經元細胞的行為出發 , 來了解人類心理活動產生的過程 。 比如人們是如何記憶、想象甚至思考的	now , all of these are new eras of cognitive neuroscience , and in this field , we're beginning to try to learn from the behaviors of individual neurons in the brain , by the billions of neurons in the human psychological processes , such as how memory , imagination or even thinking of people .
謝謝各位 。	thank you .
想象一個由合作多部門 , 多政府 , 公私力量組成的全球安全 。 這不僅是開放安全支持者的幻想 , 而是jamesstavridis , 北約最高長官的設想 , 他從分享了從現代軍事史的生動瞬間到解釋了為什麼要靠修橋而不是修牆來構築未來安全 。	imagining a global security composed by multiple branches of governments , private forces , not only an open security fantasy , but james stavridis , the highest commissioner of the north , shared the instant moments of the modern military history to explain why bridges are making safety .

我們先回顧一下20世紀吧 , 然後我們就能瞭解安全這個概念是如何為我們而工作 。	let's go back to the 20th century , and we can see how this idea of security works for us .
這裡是verdun , 一個法國的戰場 , 就在北約在比利時總部的北邊 。	this is verdun , a battlefield in france , just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .
1916年 , 在verdun這個戰場上 , 700000人在300天內被殺了 , 那就是差不多2000人一天 。	in 1916 , in verdun , 7 , 000 thousand people were killed in 300 days , just about 2 , 000 a day .
咱們繼續往前看--20世紀的安全--看到二戰 , 我們看得到在斯大林格勒保衛戰 , 300天內有二百萬人戰死 。	let's keep going forward the 20th century security you see world war ii , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .

所以我今天的主題是為了完成 " 安全 " 這個目標 , 我們不建造牆 , 而建造橋 。	so my thesis for us today is to fulfill this security , where we don't build walls and build bridges .
在歐洲有一個很著名的橋 。	there's a very famous bridge in europe .

而最近 , 也就是在近十年 , 我們開始看到這些地區開始 , 儘管有些猶豫不決 , 逐漸融合在一起 。	and more recently , in the last 10 years , we're starting to see these places start , despite hesitation and come together .
我想再次重申 , 開放式安全是關於聯絡國際的不同地區的 , 跨部門的 , 私人的和公共的 , 並且把它們透過戰略性溝通 , 在社交網上聯絡在一起 。	i want to repeat that , again , opensource security about different parts of the international , international , private and public , and connecting them through strategic communication , social networks .
所以 , 接下來我將說一些為什麼我們需要那麼做 , 因為我們的共同目標正在受到威脅 , 而且是多方面的 , 同時沒有一種威脅能被透過築牆隔離解決 。	so i'm going to talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our shared goals are threatened , and in many ways , and no threat can be solved by building walls .

當他被治好他的重度近視是 , 他突然抬頭 , 然後說: " mama , veoelmundo. "	when he was cured of his focus , he suddenly looked up , and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "

這個合作的另一部分是災後救援與後續工作 。	another part of this partnership is disaster relief and subsequent work .
這是一個美國空軍的直升機 , 它參加了2004年一個殺死250000人的海嘯的救援 。	this is a us air force helicopter participating in a tsunami in 2004 that killed 25 , 000 people .
在所有的大災難中2004年海嘯 , 250000死 , 2005年巴基斯坦地震 , 85000人死亡 , 海地地震 , 300000人死亡 , 還有最近的對於日本機器核工業的地震海嘯雙重打擊在所有這些例子中 , 我們看到了國際間 , 跨部門 , 公私結合的合作 , 這個合作與安全力量同時響應這種自然災害 。	in all major disasters in 2004 , 25 , 000 dead , pakistani earthquakes , 85 , 000 dead , haiti earthquake , 3 , 000 dead , and most recently , the earthquakes of japanese industrial nuclear industry , in all of these examples , we saw partnerships between international , interagency , private public sectors , a security force that was responsible for this kind of natural disaster .
所以這些都是我們說的開放式安全的例子 。	so these are examples of what we call opensource security .
我們結合在一起 , 來共同完成這樣的事情 。	we are all combined to do things like this together .

不 , 這是一個twitter公司發的世界地圖 。	no , it's a twitter map of the world .
紫色是微博 , 綠色是地點 ,	purple are tweet . green is location .
白色是結合 。	the white is a combination .
這很能讓人想到人口普查 , 六個人口最多的國家依次是:中國 , 印度 , facebook , 美國 , twitter , 和印尼 。	it's very reminiscent of the demographics , the six largest nations in the world in descending: china , india , facebook , the united states , twitter and indonesia .
我們要這些網幹什麼 ?	what do we want ?
我們為什麼想要在其中 ?	why do we want to be involved ?

我再舉一個例子 , 是關於資訊如何傳播的 。	i'll give you another example of how information spreads .
我在倫敦發表一個像這個的演講 。 我說 , 我對你們說 , 我在facebook上 , 加我好友吧 。	i gave a talk like this in london , and i said , i'm telling you , i'm on facebook , friend me .
觀眾在笑 。	the audience is laughing .
這是ap的一篇文章 。	this is an article in ap .
世界上有兩個地方 , 芬蘭和印尼 ,	there's two places in the world: finland and indonesia .
標題是:北約艦隊司令需要好友 。	the headline was: nato admiral needs friends .
這個故事是一個催化劑 , 明天早上我就會有上百個facebook好友請求 , 來自印尼和芬蘭 , 大多數都會說: " 司令 , 我們聽說你需要好友 , 哦 , 還有 , nato是什麼 ? "	the story is a catalyst , and tomorrow i'd have hundreds of facebook friend requests from indonesia and finland , mostly saying , " admiral , we'll hear you need a friend and oh , and what's nato ? "
是的 , 我們笑了 , 但這就是我們如何傳播資訊 , 也就是我們如何把國際 , 不同部門 , 私人和公共 , 以及那些社會網聯絡起來來創造安全 。	yes , we laugh , but that's how we're communicating information , that's how we're international , different branches , private and public , and those social networks are getting in to create security .
現在 , 讓我說一個嚴肅的訊息 。	now , let me give you a serious message .

他在蘇格蘭衛隊 ,	he's in the scots guards .
正在helmand站崗 , 在阿富汗南部 。	he's at helmand , in southern afghanistan .
我把他放出來就是想提醒我們 , 我不想讓任何人離開這間屋子 , 抱著 " 我們不需要軍事部隊 " 的想法 。	i put him here to remind us i don't want anyone to leave the room with the idea that we don't need military army .

我認為生活是一個可變電阻器 ,	i think of life as a transformable resistance .
你需要調一個數值 , 並且正像我認為我們該如何在21世紀製造安全一樣 , 我們會需要在真正的戰爭和危機中使用真正強硬的力量 , 但會有很多時候 , 就像我們已經討論的 , 我們的部隊可以使21世紀安全 , 也就是國際 , 跨部門 , 公私結合 , 的安全模式的一部分 , 透過溝通來結合起來 。	you've got to dial it up , and just like i think we're going to build security in the 21st century , we're going to need to optimize the actual hard forces and crisis , but there are many times , like we've talked about , our troops can make the 21stcentury security , the international , the public , part of the security model , through communication .
在結束時 , 我想說在今天早些時候聽到的關於維基百科的一些東西 。 我經常用維基百科查一些東西 , 就像你所知道的 , 維基百科不是靠12個聰明的人把自己關在屋子裡寫文章建立的 。	i'd like to close by saying that i heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up things , and as you know , wikipedia is not built on 12 smart people locking themselves in a room writing articles .
維基百科是靠每天數萬人的更新 , 數百萬人的提取資訊而建立的 。	wikipedia is relying on tens of thousands of people every day to extract information from millions of people .
這完美的說明了沒有一個人能比共同思考更聰明 。	it's a perfect illustration that no one of us could think together more brilliantly than think together .
沒有一個人 , 沒有一個聯盟 , 沒有一個國家 , 能有我們共同思考更睿智 。	no one , no one alliance , no one nation , none of us are as smart as all of us thinking together .
維基百科的宣言很簡單:建立一個能人人自由共享所有知識的世界 。	the wikipedia manifesto is simple: build a world where every human being can freely share all knowledge .
所以 , 我想說 , 透過結合國際 , 多部門 , 公私力量 , 戰略通訊在一起 , 在21世紀 , 我們能創造共同的安全 。	so i would like to say that by combining international , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in the 21st century , we can create the same security .
非常感謝 。	thank you very much .
